Whaniver he saa thair faith, he saed, “Ma freen, yer sïns ïs aa forgien.”  Tha maistèrs o tha Laa an tha Pharisees stairtit taakin amang thairsels. “Wha daes he thïnk he ïs, taakin sitch blesphemie? Wha can forgie sïns but God alane?”  Jesus knowed whut thair thochts wur, an saed tae thaim, “Hoo cum yis ir thïnkin laik thïs?  Is ït aisier tae say, ‘Yer sïns ir forgien’, or tae say ‘Get up an waak’?  But noo ye'll see that tha Sinn o Man haes tha pooer tae forgie sïns here on irth.” Jesus then saed tae tha man that haed bin paralysed, “Get up, tak yer bed wi ye, an gang awa hame!”  An richt awa he got up afore thaim, gethert up hïs beddin, an went aff hame, praisin God.  The' cud harlie believe ït, an the' gien glorie tae God, yit at tha same time the' felt feart an saed, “We hae saen thïngs theday that ir ower ocht!” Eftèr thïs, Jesus went oot an saa a tex man bi tha name o Levi, sïttin ïn hïs hut. An Jesus saed tae hïm, “Follae me!”  Levi ris up, left aa behin hïm, an follaed Jesus.  An Levi layed on a bïg spreed ïn hïs ain hoose fer Jesus, an thair wus a hale lock o tex men an tha laik thair, roon tha table wi thaim.  But tha maistèrs o tha Laa an tha Pharisees wus muttèrin tae tha follaers o Jesus, “Fer why ir ye aitin an drïnkin wi tex men an sïnners?”  An Jesus saed tae thaim, “Fowk that ir hale an hairtie dïnnae need a doctèr, but seeck fowk dae!  A hinnae cum fer tae caa guid leevin fowk tae repentance, but A hae cum tae caa sïnners.” Some fowk saed tae hïm, “Jhone's follaers ir aye fastin an prayin, an sae dae tha follaers o tha Pharisees, but your yins ïs aye aitin an drïnkin!”  But Jesus saed tae thaim, “Ye cannae mak waddin guests fast while tha bridegruim ïs wi thaim.  Thair'll cum a day but, whaniver tha bridegruim wull be tuk awa frae thaim, an that'll be tha time the' wull fast.”  He toul thaim anither parable: “Naebodie taks a piece o claith frae a new cóat tae patch an oul yin. If he daes, tha new patch wull pu awa frae tha oul, an forbye the' wudnae match.  An naebodie pits new wine ïntae oul wineskïns. Fer ïf ye dae, tha new wine wull brust tha oul skïns, tha wine wull spïll oot an tha skïns wull be ruint.  Na, ye hae tae pit new wine ïntae new skïns, [then baith wull be aa richt].  Forbye, naebodie eftèr haein drunk oul wine, wud richt awa be lukkin new wine. Fer he wud say, ‘Tha oul wine ïs bettèr.’ ” Cum twa Sabbaths eftèr thïs, Jesus wus gaun throu tha coarnfiels an hïs follaers pluckt tha heids aff tha coarn tae ait, giein thaim a rub atween thair hans.  An some o tha Pharisees axt thaim, “Hoo cum yis ir daein whut's agin tha Laa on tha Sabbath day?”  Jesus gien tha answer, “Hae ye no read whut Davit daen whaniver hïm an hïs freens wus hung'rie?  Hoo he gaed ïntae tha Hoose o God, an tuk an et tha halie showbreid, an gien ït tae thaim that wus wi hïm forbye? Shair that wus agin tha Laa fer oniebodie but tha preeshts!”  An he saed tae thaim, “Tha Sinn o Man ïs Loard o tha Sabbath anaa.” Then on anither Sabbath he gaed ïntae tha Meetin Hoose tae taich tha fowk, an thair wus a man thair an hïs richt han wus wuthert.  Tha maistèrs o tha Laa an tha Pharisees kep thair een on Jesus tae see wud he hail on tha Sabbath, sae as tae hae sumthin agin hïm.  But he kent richt weel thair thochts an saed tae tha man wi tha baad han, “Stan up whar the' can aa see ye.” An up he got.  Then Jesus saed tae thaim, “Daes tha Laa say ye shud dae guid or dae ïll on tha Sabbath? Shud ye save life or dae awa wi ït?”  An lukkin roon at thaim aa, he saed tae tha man, “Streetch oot yer han!”; an he dïd, an hïs han cum as guid as tha ither yin.  The' wur aa richt an maad an wur colloguin wi yin anither whut the' cud dae wi Jesus. Bye an bye Jesus went oot tae a muntin fer tae pray tae God, an he kep at ït tha hale nicht lang.  An whaniver ït wus day, he caad hïs follaers tae hïm an he waaled oot twal o thaim, an gien thaim tha name o “Possels”:  Simon, that he caad Petèr forbye, an hïs brither Andra; Jeames an Jhone; Phïlip an Bartholomew;  Mattha an Tammas; Jeames, tha sinn o Alphaeus; Simon, tha yin the' caad a zealot;  Judas, Jeames's sinn; an Judas Iscariot, tha yin that bethrayed Jesus latèr on. An he cum doon frae tha muntin wi thaim, an tuk hïs stance on a flet bït o grun; an a hale crood o hïs follaers, alang wi a wile thrang o fowk oot o Judea, an Jerusalem, an frae alang tha shores o Tyre an Sidon, cum tae hear hïm an tae be cured o thair ailments.  An tha yins vext sair wi ïll spïrits wus aa cured.  An tha hale crood o fowks wantit tae touch hïm acause a pooer o guid wus cumin oot o hïm an curin thaim aa. An Jesus, wi hïs een on hïs follaers saed, “Blisst ir tha puir, fer yours ïs tha Kïngdom o God.  Blisst ir you that's hung'rie noo, fer yis wull get yer fïll. Blisst ir you that's greetin noo, fer yis wull be lachin then.  Blisst ir you whaniver fowk hait ye or gie ye tha coul shoodèr, baadmooth ye or blekin yer name, on accoont o tha Sinn o Man.  Be richt gled on that day an gie a lep fer joy, fer yis hae a pooerfu reward waitin fer ye ïn heiven; fer thair faithers daen tha same tae tha proaphits.  But sorra tae you weel-aff fowk, fer ye hae got aa ye ir gettin!  Sorra tae you that's fu noo, fer yis wull be hung'rie. Sorra tae you that ir lachin, fer yis wull be greetin an sorrafu.  Wae faa yis whan aa fowk spakes weel o ye, fer thair faithers daen tha same wi tha fauss proaphits. But A'm sayin tae yous that's lïstenin: Love yer faes, dae guid tae thaim that haits ye.  Bliss thaim that curses ye, an pray fer thaim that wushes ye ïll wull.  An ïf a bodie gies ye a slap on tha cheek, turn tha ither side til hïm forbye. An ïf a bodie ïs lukkin yer tap-cóat aff ye, let hïm hae yer shirt as weel.  If oniebodie axes ye fer ocht, gie ït tae thaim, an dïnnae be lukkin ït bak.  An jist dae tae ithers whut yis wud want thaim tae dae tae yersels. An ïf yis onlie love thaim at loves you, thair's naethin parteeclar aboot that. Even sïnners love tha yins that love thaim.  An ïf yis dae guid tae thaim at dae guid tae yersels, whut credit ïs that tae yis? Sïnners dae jist tha same.  An ïf yis onlie lenn tae thaim at yis ir hopin tae get ït bak frae, thair's nae thenks ïn that, fer even sïnners lenn tae sïnners, sae as tae get bak tha same agane.  But love yer faes, dae guid an lenn, no hopin tae get oniethin bak; an yis wull hae great reward an wull be sinns o tha Maist Heich, fer he ïs kine tae tha ungratefu an tha wïckit.  Sae be merciefu, jist as yer Faither ïs merciefu. Dïnnae judge ithers, an ye'll no be judged yersels; dïnnae condemn an yis'll no be condemned; forgie an yis'll be forgien.  Gie an yis'll be gien tae; a guid misure, preest doon, shuk thegither an skailin ower wull be gien tae yis. Fer tha misure yis gie wull be tha misure yis get bak.” An Jesus spauk a parable tae thaim: “Can tha blin lead tha blin? Wull the' no baith faa ïntae tha sheuch?  A follaer ïs no abain hïs taicher, but whaniver he ïs weel lairnt, he wull be jist laik hïs taicher.  An why dae ye see tha skelf ïn yer brither's ee, but ye dïnnae see tha plenk ïn yer ain ee?  Hoo can ye say tae yer brither, ‘Cum here brither, let me tak tha skelf oot o yer ee’, an yit ye cannae see tha plenk ïn yer ain ee? Ye oul hippycrate ye, pu tha plenk oot o yer ain ee furst, an then ye'll be able tae see proper, tae tak tha skelf oot o yer brither's ee! A guid tree daesnae gie rotten fruit, ner daes a rotten tree gie guid fruit.  Ye know iverie tree bi ïts ain fruit. Ye dïnnae pïck fïgs frae a thoarn büsh ner grapes frae a blekberrie büsh.  A guid man brïngs guid oot o tha guidness stored ïn hïs hairt, an a evil man brïngs evil oot o tha evil ïn hïs hairt. Fer whutiver hïs hairt ïs fu o, that's whut cums oot o hïs mooth. An why caa me ‘Loard, Loard’, an no dae whut A say?  Whaiver cums tae me an hears these wurds o mine an heeds thaim, A'll show ye whut he ïs laik.  He's laik a man that bigged hïs hoose, an he dug deep an set tha fïttins on a roak, an whaniver tha rïver wus ïn fu spate an swep agin tha hoose, ït cudnae shïft ït, fer ït wus set on a roak.  But tha yin that hears whut A say an daesnae dae ït, ïs laik a man that bigged hïs hoose wi nae fundations ava, an whaniver tha rush o wattèr hut ït, tha hale hoose brauk apairt at yinst.” Whan Jesus haed daen taakin tae tha fowk, he gaed ïntae Capernaum.  Thair wus thïs centurion thonner haed a sarvin man he thocht weel o, that wus seeck an deein.  Whan he heerd tell o Jesus, he axt some eldèrs o tha Jews tae fin oot ïf Jesus wud cum an mak tha sarvin man weel agane.  Whan the' cum tae Jesus, the' kep beggin hïm, sayin, “Ye shud dae sumthin fer thïs man, fer he wus tarrible fand o us Jews, an he even bigged a Meetin Hoose fer iz. He desarves ye tae dae thïs fer hïm.”  Sae Jesus gan awa wi thaim. Whan he wus nearhan tha hoose, tha centurion sent freens oot fer tae tell hïm, “Loard, dïnnae bother cumin onie neardèr, fer A'm no fït tae hae ye cum unnèr ma ruif.  It's no fer tha laiks o me tae cum tae you. But jist say tha wurd, an ma sarvin man wull be weel agane.  Fer A ken hoo tae tak oardèrs; A hae sodgers unnèr me as weel. A tell yin tae gang an he gangs, an anither yin tae cum, an he cums. A tell ma sarvin man, ‘Dae thïs!’ an he daes ït.”  Whan Jesus heerd thïs, he wus stoondit at hïm, an he turnt roon tae tha crood cumin eftèr hïm an saed, “A'm tellin ye, A niver fun oniebodie wi sitch faith ïn aa Israel.”  Whan tha freens that wur sent oot cum bak tae tha centurion's hoose, the' fun tha sarvin man weel agane. Tha nixt day, Jesus went tae a toon caad Nain. Hïs follaers an a bïg crood o fowk cum alang wi hïm.  Whan he cum near tha gate ïntae tha toon, ït happent that the' wur cairryin oot a deid man, a weeda wumman's ainlie sinn. An a bïg crood wus follaein hir oot frae tha toon.  Whan tha Loard lukt at hir, he tuk peetie on hir, an he toul hir, “Dïnnae greet”.  He cum ower an püt hïs han on tha coffin, an tha yins that wur cairtin ït stapt. He saed, “Cum on, young man, up ye get!”  Tha deid man sut up an stairtit tae taak, an Jesus gien hïm bak tae hïs mither.  The' wur aa hairt-scarred, an the' praised God, sayin, “A pooerfu proaphit haes ris up frae amang iz. God haes cum tae halp hïs fowk oot.”  Whut Jesus daen that day wus tha taak o tha hale o Judea an aa tha kintrie roon aboot. Jhone heerd aboot aa thïs frae hïs follaers.  An he caad fer twa o thaim an sent thaim tae tha Loard fer tae ax, “Wud you be tha Yin that wus supposed tae cum, or shud we be lukkin oot fer some ither bodie?”  The' cum tae Jesus an saed, “Jhone tha Baptiser sent iz tae ax ye, ‘Ir you tha Yin that wus supposed tae cum?  Or shud we be lukkin oot fer some ither bodie?’”  At that oor, Jesus made a lock o seeck fowk weel agane frae thair ailments. He rïd thaim o ïll spïrits, an he made fowk that wur blin able tae see agane.  He toul Jhone's follaers, “Gang bak an gie Jhone an accoont o whut ye hae saen an heerd. Blin fowk can see noo, lameters can waak, fowk wi leprosie ir makkit weel. Deef fowk can hear. Tha deid leeve agane. An tha Guid News ïs praicht tae tha puir.  An blisst ïs tha yin that daesnae misdoot me.” Whan Jhone's messengers went awa, Jesus stairtit tae taak tae tha croods aboot Jhone. He axt thaim, “Whut dïd ye gang oot ïntae tha wuldèrness fer tae see? Wus ït tae see tha rushes sweein ïn tha wun?  If no, whut dïd ye thïnk ye wud see oot thair? A man aa rigged oot ïn fancie claes? Na, fowk that's weel dresst an leevin ït up, ït's ïn kïngs' palaces ye wull fin them.  Sae whut dïd yis gae oot fer tae see? Wus ït a proaphit? Ay, A tell ye, an faur mair ner a proaphit.  Thïs ïs tha yin tha Scrïptures taak aboot whaniver the' say: ‘Lïsten, A'll senn oot ma messenger aheid o ye; he wull mak readie tha wye afore ye.’  A tell ye, thair wus niver a bettèr man boarn o a wumman ner Jhone, an yit tha yin that ïs laist ïn tha Kïngdom o God ïs a bettèr man ner hïm.”  (Aa tha fowk, even tha tex men, whaniver the' haed heerd thïs, the' knowed fer sartin God's wye wus richt, fer the' haed bin baptised bi Jhone.  But tha Pharisees an tha laayers haednae hoult wi God's plan fer thaim. They haednae bin baptised bi Jhone.) Jesus axt thaim, “Whut wull A say aboot tha fowk noo-a-days? Whut kine o fowk ir the'?  The' ir laik weans sïttin doon at tha mairket, caain oot tae yin anither, ‘We played tha whustle fer ye, an ye wudnae daunce. We sung a dirge tae ye, an ye wudnae greet.’  Fer Jhone tha Baptiser wusnae ïntae aitin breid ner drïnkin wine whaniver he cum, an ye say, ‘Thair's a baad spïrit ïn hïm.’  But tha Sinn o Man cum aitin an drïnkin, an ye say, ‘Wud ye luk at hïm, he's a glutton, an he's tarrible fand o tha drïnk, sae he ïs - tha freen o tex men an wrangdaers!’  But whan fowk daes whut's richt, the' prove tha wusdom o God's wyes.” Noo yin o tha Pharisees axt Jesus fer hïs dennèr, sae Jesus went hame wi hïm fer a bite tae ait an tuk hïs place at tha boord.  An thair wus thïs wumman wi a baad name aboot tha toon, an whaniver she heerd that Jesus wus aitin at tha Pharisee's hoose, she brocht a wee crock o scent wi hir,  an as she wus behin hïm greetin, hir tears stairtit tae faa on Jesus's feet. Tha wumman dryed hïs feet wi tha hair o hir heid, an she kïsst thaim as she poored tha scent ower thaim.  Noo whaniver tha Pharisee that haed axt hïm tae cum saen thïs, he thocht tae hissel, “If thïs man wus a proaphit, he shud hae kent whut soart o a wumman thïs ïs that toucht hïm. He shud a knowed she's a baad wumman.”  Jesus toul hïm, “A want tae tell ye sumthin, Simon.” Simon saed, “Maistèr, whut hae ye tae tell me?”  “Thair wus thïs man,” saed Jesus, “that wud hae lent siller tae fowk. An twa men owed hïm. Tha yin owed hïm five hunnèr siller coins, an tha ither owed hïm fïftie.  Noo whan nane o tha twa haed eneuch siller tae pye hïm bak, tha money-lender toul thaim ït wus aa richt, an he lut thaim aff. Whut yin o thaim, dae ye thïnk, wud laik hïm tha maist?”  Simon saed, “Tha yin that he lut aff that owed hïm tha maist, A suppose.” Says Jesus, “Ay, that's richt. Ye hae saed ït.”  Then Jesus lukt ower at tha wumman an saed tae Simon, “Dae ye see thïs wumman? A cum ïntae yer hoose, an ye niver gien me onie wattèr fer ma feet. But she haes waasht ma feet wi hir tears, an dichtit thaim wi hir hair.  Ye dïdnae show that ye wur gled tae see me bi giein me a kïss, but thïs wumman haesnae stapt kïssin ma feet sin A cum ïn!  Ye niver even thocht o pittin a drap o oyle on ma heid, but thïs wumman haes poored scent aa ower ma feet.  A tell ye, hir monie wrangdaeins haes bin forgien, fer she haes showed that much love tae me. Tha yin that haes bin forgien a wee bït, wull onlie love a wee bït.”  An Jesus saed tae tha wumman, “Yer wrangdaeins ir forgien.”  Tha ither fowk thair at tha table stairtit tae taak amang thairsels, sayin, “Whut kine o man ïs thïs, that can e'en forgie wrangdaeins?”  Then Jesus saed tae tha wumman, “Yer faith haes saved ye. Gang weel!” Eftèr thïs, Jesus trevelt roon aa tha toons an vïllages, praichin an tellin o tha Guid News o tha Kïngdom o God, an tha twal wus wi hïm.  Forbye, thair wur sartin weemen that haed bin cured o wïckit spïrits an ailments. Thair wus Mary, caad Magdalene; seiven ïll spïrits cum oot o hir,  an Johanna, tha guidwife o Chuza that run Herod's hoose, an Susanna, an monie mair that wur aye giein whut the' haed tae luk eftèr Jesus. Noo a wile thrang o fowk cum frae toon eftèr toon tae gether roon hïm, an he toul thaim thïs parable:  “Thair wus thïs fairmer went oot tae saa seed, an as he wus skailin ït, some drapt doon alang tha pad, an ït got waakit iver, an tha wile burds peckt ït up.  Some faad on roakie grun, an ït wus nae shuiner abraird, tae ït wuthert awa fer want o wattèr.  An some faad doon amang thoarns an breers, an tha thoarns sprung up, tuk ower, an chokt ït.  An ither seed faad on guid grun, an ït growed weel, an tha hairst wus guid, aboot a hunnèr times mair than wus saad.” Whan he haed toul thaim aa thïs, he caad oot, “Let hïm that haes ears ïn hïs heid tak tent!” An hïs follaers axt, “Whut's thïs parable aboot?”  An he saed tae thaim, “Tae you God haes gien an unnèrstannin o tha saicrets o hïs Kïngdom. But tae tha ithers A taak ïn parables: these fowk micht aye be lukkin, but the' niver see; an aye lïstenin, but the' niver unnèrstan.  Noo here's tha mainin o tha parable: Tha seed ïs tha wurd o God.  Tha seed that faad doon nixt tha pad stans fer tha fowk that hears tha wurd, but then alang cums tha Deil, an he taks ït oot o thair hairts, sae that the' ir stapt frae believin an cannae be saved.  Tha seed on tha roak stans fer tha yins that gie ear til God's wurd an tak ït ïn wi a gled hairt, but ït haes nae ruit an daesnae houl wi thaim. Fer whan haird times cum alang, the' gie up an the' hae nae mair mine o ït.  An tha seed that fell amang tha thoarns, that's laik fowk that hears tha wurd o God, an the' cairrie on fer a weethin; but ïn tha enn, aa tha warl's bothers, tha catter an tha guid times staps thaim growein up strecht an sonsie.  But tha seed that faad on guid grun, that's laik fowk that ir warthie an guid, an gie ear til tha wurd o God; the' houl ït ïn thair hairts, til ïn tha enn the' reap a rich hairst. Naebodie lichts a lamp an pits a jar ower ït, or pits ït unnèr a bed. Ye set ït oot whar fowk can see ït whan the' cum ïn.  Fer thair's naethin hïd, that wull no be toul; an thair's naethin püt awa, that wull no be brocht oot ïntae tha apen.  Mine hoo ye lïsten. Fer hïm that haes plentie wull be gien mair. An hïm that haes lïttle, even whut he thïnks he haes wull be tuk awa frae hïm.” Noo Jesus' mither an hïs brithers cum tae see hïm, but the' cudnae get near tae hïm fer aa tha crood o fowk.  Jesus wus toul, “Yer mither an brithers ir waitin ootbye, lukkin tae see ye.”  But he cum bak wi, “Ma mither an ma brithers ir tha yins that lïsten tae tha Wurd o God, an follae ït!” Yin day, Jesus got ïntae a bóat wi hïs follaers, an he saed tae thaim, “C'mon an we'll gang ower tae tha ither side o tha loch”. Sae the' püt oot.  Noo while the' wur oot on tha wattèr, Jesus lay doon fer a sleep. An ït begun tae get wile stoarmie, an tha bóat begun tae tak on wattèr. An ït wus tarrible dangeris.  Hïs follaers went up tae hïm an waakent hïm. “Dominie, dominie!” the' caad oot, “we'll be droont!” An Jesus ris, an he chackt tha blowstèrin wun an waves. Aa at yinst tha wun drapt, an tha stoarm wus ower.  “Whar ïs yer faith?” he axt thaim. An the' wur feart, an the' wunnèrt, an the' saed tae yin anither, “Whut kine o a man ïs thïs, that can mak e'en tha wun an tha waves dae as he bïds thaim!” Jesus an hïs follaers cum tae tha lan whar tha Gerasenes leeved, strecht ower tha loch frae Galilee.  An whaniver he wus gettin oot o tha bóat, thair wus thïs man cum up tae hïm frae tha toon. He wus fu o demons, an haed bin rinnin roon fer a lang time wi naethin on hïm, an leevin ïn tha graveyaird rether than a hoose.  Whan he saen Jesus, he faad at hïs feet an guldèrt, “Whut ïs ït ye ir eftèr wi me, Jesus, sinn o tha maist heich God? A'm beggin ye, quït tormentin me!”  Fer ye see, Jesus haed bïd tha ïll spïrit tae lea hïm alane. Betimes ït haed made hïm brek awa frae hïs gairds an tha chains the' haed bun hïm up wi, an ït haed driv hïm oot ïntae tha wiles.  An Jesus axt hïm, “Whut dae the' caa ye?” “A'm caad Legion,” saed he; fer monie demons haed tuk houl o hïm.  An tha demons kep on beggin Jesus no tae be püt ïntae tha Blek Pït.  Noo a bïg herd o pïgs wus oot hokin fer food on tha braeside, an tha demons begged tae be sent ïntae tha pïgs. An Jesus allooed ït.  Sae tha demons cum oot o Legion, an the' went ïntae tha pïgs. Tha herd tuk aff doon tha hïll, heid furst ïntae tha loch, an tha hale lock wus droont. An whaniver tha yins that wur lukkin eftèr tha pïgs saen whut haed happent, the' run aff an toul iveriebodie ïn tha toon an kintrie roon aboot.  An tha fowk that heerd cum oot tae see fer thairsels. An whan the' cum tae Jesus, the' fun tha man tha demons haed cum oot o. Legion wus sïttin thair quait at tha feet o Jesus. He haed hïs claes on, an wus ïn hïs richt mine. An the' wur wile scarred.  An thaim that haed saen tha hailin o tha man wi tha demons, toul tha ithers aa aboot ït.  An aa tha fowk frae tha lan o tha Gadarenes  begged Jesus tae gang awa, fer the' wur wile feart. Sae Jesus heidit aff tae tha bóat, fer tae gae awa bak ower the loch.  Tha man tha demons went oot o besocht Jesus that he cud gae alang wi hïm, but Jesus toul hïm tae lea, an saed,  “Gang awa hame, an tell tha fowk aboot tha great thïngs God haes daen fer ye.” Sae tha man went hame, an he toul tha hale toon whut Jesus haed daen fer hïm. Noo whaniver Jesus cum bak, a crood o fowk bïd hïm walcum, fer the' wur aa waitin on hïm.  Then a man caad Jairus, a heidyin o tha Meetin Hoose, cum an faad doon at Jesus' feet, beggin wi hïm tae cum tae hïs hoose,  fer hïs ainlie dochtèr, a wee lass o twal yeir oul, wus deein. But as Jesus wus gaun thair, tha thrang wus croodin roon hïm. An thair wus thïs wumman amang thaim that haed bother wi bleedin fer twal yeir, but naebodie cud dae oniethin fer hir.  She cum ahint Jesus, an she toucht tha enn o hïs cloke, an strecht awa tha bleedin stapt.  “Wha toucht me?” axt Jesus. Whan naebodie owned up tae ït, Petèr saed, “Dominie, fowk ir püshin an shuvin aa roon ye [an ye ir wunnèrin wha toucht ye?!]”.  Saed Jesus, “Summodie haes toucht me! Fer A felt tha pooer gang oot o me!”  Tha wumman, seein that she cudnae hide, cum an faad doon afeart an trimmlin at hïs feet. An afore tha hale fowk, she toul whut fer she haed toucht hïm, an hoo she haed bin makkit weel at yinst.  Then Jesus saed, “Dochtèr, yer faith haes hailt ye.  Fair ye weel!” Tha wurds wusnae richt aff Jesus' tung, whan thïs man cum frae tha hame o tha heidyin o tha Meetin Hoose, an saed tae hïm, “Jairus, yer dochtèr ïs deid; dïnnae bother tha maistèr onie mair.”  Whan Jesus heerd thïs, he toul hïm, “Dïnnae be feart! Jist believe, an she wull be hailt!”  An whan Jesus cum tae tha hoose, tha yins he allooed tae cum ïn wi hïm wur Petèr, Jhone an Jeames, alang wi tha faither an mither o tha wee lass.  Noo the' wur aa greetin an wailin fer hir, but Jesus saed, “Be quait! She's no deid, she's jist sleepin.”  An the' stairtit tae lach, fer the' kent she wus deid.  Hooaniver, Jesus tuk hir bi tha han an caad oot, “Cum on chile, up ye git!”  An hir spïrit cum bak, an at yinst she got up. An he toul thaim tae gie hir a bite tae ait.  Tha mither an faither cudnae believe thair een. But Jesus toul thaim on nae accoont tae say tae oniebodie whut haed happent. Eftèr Jesus caad hïs twal follaers thegither, he gien thaim pooer iver aa tha demons, an pooer tae cure aa kines o disaises.  An he sent thaim oot tae praich tha Kïngdom o God an tae hail tha seeck.  An he toul thaim, “Tak naethin wi ye fer tha róad, nether stav tae studie ye, ner baag tae cairrie ocht ïn, ner breid, ner siller, an nae spare claes.  Whan ye gang ïntae a hoose, stap ower thair tae ït's time tae tak yer lave o that toon.  An whar ye'r no walcum, ye'r tae lea that toon, an ye'r tae dicht aff e'en tha stour o yer feet, as a wutness an warnin tae thaim.”  An aff the' went, gaun frae vïllage tae vïllage, praichin tha Guid News an hailin thair an thonner. Noo whan Herod tha Tetrarch heerd aboot aa tha thïngs that Jesus wus daein, he wus fair fasht, acause some fowk saed that Jhone tha Baptiser wus ris frae tha deid.  Some thocht that yin o tha oul-time proaphits haed cum bak tae life, an ithers thocht ït wus mebbe Elijah.  But Herod saed, “A haed tha heid tuk aff Jhone. But wha's thon A'm hearin sitch thïngs aboot?” An he wus ower enxious tae see Jesus. An tha possels, whan the' cum bak, toul Jesus aboot aa tha thïngs the' haed daen, an he tuk thaim aff bi thair lane tae a [quait place near tha] toon caad Bethsaida. But tha croods kent thïs an follaed hïm. An he bïd thaim walcum an taakt tae thaim o tha Kïngdom o God, an brocht hailin tae thaim that haed need o ït.  Noo at dailygan, tha Twal cum tae hïm an saed, “Senn aa tha croods o fowk awa, sae that the' can gang an fin ludgins an a bite tae ait fer thairsels ïn tha clachans an fairm hooses roon aboot. Fer we'r ïn a richt oot o tha wye place here.”  But Jesus toul thaim, “Yous gie thaim sumthin tae ait.” An the' saed, “We hae naethin but five bannocks an twa fïsh. Or mebbe we shud try an buy sumthin fer aa these fowk?!”  Thair wur aboot five thoosan men. An Jesus saed tae hïs follaers, “Mak thaim aa sït doon ïn groups o aboot fïftie.”  Sae the' bïd thaim aa sït doon.  Then he tuk tha five bannocks an tha twa fïsh, an lukkin up tae heiven, he blisst ït an brauk ït, an he kep giein ït tae hïs follaers tae han oot tae aa tha fowk.  Eftèr the' haed aa et thair fïll, the' gethert up aa tha wee bïts, eneuch tae fïll twal creels. Yin day Jesus wus prayin alane, tha mair hïs follaers wus nearhan. An he axt thaim, “Wha dae tha croods say that A am?”  The' saed, “A wheen o fowk say Jhone tha Baptiser, some wud say Elijah, an ithers agane say that yin o tha proaphits frae lang syne haes cum bak tae life.”  “An whut aboot yersels?” he axt. “Wha dae yous say that A am?” Petèr spauk up, “You ir tha Christ o God.”  An he gien thaim a warnin, an bïd thaim no tae tell oniebodie. An he toul thaim, “Tha Sinn o Man maun suffer monies a thïng an be gien tha coul shoodèr bi tha eldèrs, tha heid preeshts an tha maistèrs o tha Laa. An he maun be püt tae deith an be ris up tae life on tha thurd day.” An he saed tae thaim aa, “If oniebodie wants tae follae eftèr me, he maun ferget aboot hissel aathegither, tak up hïs cross iverie day, an stïck clase tae me.  Fer whaiver wants tae save hïs life wull loass ït, but hïm that loasses hïs life on accoont o me wull save ït.  Fer whut guid ïs ït fer a bodie tae get tha hale warl, an yit desthroy hissel bodie an sowl?  Fer ïf oniebodie ïs no wullin tae stan up fer me an ma wurds, then tha Sinn o Man wull no stan up fer hïm whan he cums ïn hïs glorie, an tha glorie o hïs Faither an tha halie angels tae.  A'm tellin ye strecht, thair's yins stud here theday that fer sartin wull no dee afore the' see tha Kïngdom o God.” Yin day, aboot echt days eftèr he haed saed these thïngs, he tuk Petèr, Jeames an Jhone up ïntae a muntin tae pray.  An whaniver he wus prayin, tha hale luk o hïm wus changed, an hïs claes wus glancin white turnt.  An then thair wus these twa men taakin wi hïm - ït wus Moses an Elijah,  fu o heivenlie splendour, an the' taakt aboot tha wye he wud dee ïn Jerusalem.  But Petèr an tha ithers wi hïm haed drapt aff tae sleep, an whaniver the' waakent up the' saa hïs glorie an tha twa men stannin wi hïm.  An as tha twa men wus leain Jesus, Petèr saed, “Dominie, A'm gled we ir here tae see thïs. Cum on an we'll big thrie shiltèrs, yin fer you, yin fer Moses an yin fer Elijah.” But he wus jist rannèrin.  Whan Petèr wus taakin, a clood cum doon an the' wur loast ïn ït. An the' wur hairt-scarred whan that happent.  An a voice cum oot o tha clood sayin, “Thïs ïs ma Sinn, tha Yin A hae chose. Lïsten tae hïm!”  Whan tha voice haed stapt taakin, the' lukt an thair wus nae yin thair but Jesus. An at tha time, the' dïdnae breathe a wurd o whut the' haed saen tae onie yin. Nixt day, whan the' haed cum doon aff tha hïll, a hale crood o fowk cum tae meet hïm,  an thïs man caad oot frae tha crood, “Maistèr, A beg ye, wud ye tak a luk at ma sinn? He's tha ainlie chile A hae.  An a wïckit spïrit ïs aye takkin houl o hïm, an whan ït daes, he lets oot a guldèr, an he stairts tae fït an foam at tha mooth, an ït's onlie eftèr he's bin hurt baad that ït leas hïm.  A brocht hïm tae yer follaers tae rïd hïm o tha spïrit, but the' cudnae dae ït.”  An Jesus saed, “You fowk ir sae faithless an aisie led! Hoo lang wull A be wi ye afore yis believe? Hoo lang dae A hae tae pit up wi ye? Brïng yer sinn here tae me!”  Jist as tha wee lad wus cumin, he faad doon tae tha grun fïttin, an Jesus gien tha wïckit spïrit a richt barjin, an hailt tha wee lad an gien hïm bak tae hïs faither.  The' wur aa pure dumfoonèrt at tha pooer o God. But whiles the' aa wunnèrt at tha thïngs Jesus dïd, he saed tae hïs follaers,  “Wull yis tak heed tae whut A'm sayin, an let ït sink ïn. Tha Sinn o Man ïs gaun tae be pit ïntae tha pooer o men.”  But the' dïdnae unnèrstan whut he wus sayin, an the' cudnae fethom ït oot; yit the' wur feart tae ax hïm whut he meent. Then the' begun queeryin amang thairsels wha wud be tha maist thocht o amang thaim.  An Jesus, knowin whut the' wur thïnkin, tuk a wean an set hïm doon aside hïm.  An he saed tae thaim, “Whaiver maks thïs chile walcum ïn ma name, walcums me, an oniebodie that walcums me, walcums hïm that sent me. Tha yin regairdit o nae accoont amang ye, that's tha yin that'll hae tha maist honour.” Jhone saed tae hïm, “Dominie, we saa a bodie drivin oot demons ïn your name an we made hïm stap, fer he ïsnae yin o us.”  But Jesus saed, “Dae nae sitch thïng, fer oniebodie that's no agin ye ïs wi ye.” An as tha time wus cumin roon fer Jesus tae lea tha irth, he set hissel tae gang up tae Jerusalem.  An he sent some messengers on up aheid o hïm, an the' went aff tae a Samaritan vïllage fer tae mak readie fer hïs cumin.  But tha fowk thonner wudnae mak hïm walcum, acause the' cud see he wus bent on gaun tae Jerusalem. Whaniver Jeames an Jhone heerd thïs, the' saed, “Loard, let iz caa doon fire frae heiven an burn thaim aa up, [jist as Elijah dïd.]”  But Jesus toul thaim aff, [an saed, “Ye hae nae unnèrstannin ava,  Fer tha Sinn o Man haesnae cum tae desthroy men's lifes, but tae save thaim.”] Sae the' went on tae anither vïllage. An sae ït wus, as the' wur on thair wye, thïs bodie saed tae Jesus, “A wull follae ye, nae mettèr whar ye'r fer!”  Saed Jesus tae hïm, “Foxes hae holes an burds hae nests, but tha Sinn o Man haes naewhar he can caa hame.”  An he saed tae anither yin, “Follae me”. But he saed, “Loard, let me gang an burie ma faither furst.”  But Jesus saed bak tae hïm, “Let tha deid burie thair ain deid, but awa you gang an praich tha Kïngdom o God.”  An yit anither yin saed, “Loard, A'll follae ye, but let me gang an say aa ma guidbyes tae ma fowk bak hame.”  But Jesus toul hïm, “Oniebodie that stairts tae ploo, an keeps lukkin behin hïm, ïs nae guid tae tha Kïngdom o God.” Eftèr aa thïs, tha Loard caad oot seiventie mair follaers an sent thaim oot aheid o hïm, twa bi twa, tae aa tha toons an places whar he wus gaun tae vïsit hissel.  An he saed tae thaim, “Thair's a gran hairst waitin, but thair's no monie warkers tae gether ït ïn. Sae keep on axin tha Loard o tha hairst tae senn oot mair warkers ïntae hïs hairvest fiel.  Noo, awa yis gang, but mine ye, A'm sennin yis oot laik lambs amang wolfs.  Dïnnae cairrie a pooch ner a baag, ner e'en spare shune, an dïnnae stap tae blether wi oniebodie on tha róad.  Whutiver hoose yis gang ïntae, say furst, ‘God bliss thïs hoose wi peace.’  If thair's peace-lovin fowk thair, yer blissin wull bide wi thaim; an ïf thair ïsnae onie, yer blissin wull cum bak tae ye.  Stap ïn tha yin hoose, an ait an drïnk whut the' set afore ye, fer a warker ïs warth hïs wages. Dïnnae flït aboot frae hoose tae hoose.  An whaniver yis gang ïntae a toon, ïf the' bïd yis walcum, ait aa the' set afore ye.  An hail tha seeck fowk thair, an say tae thaim, ‘Tha Kïngdom o God haes cum nearhan ye.’  But ïf ye gang ïntae a toon an the' dïnnae bïd ye walcum, gang oot ïntae tha raas an tell thaim,  ‘E'en tha stour o yer toon that clegs oor feet, we dicht ït aff as a warnin tae ye, but we'll hae ye know that tha Kïngdom o God haes cum nearhan ye.’  A tell ye, tha fowk o Sodom wull be bettèr aff on tha Day o Reckonin ner that toon. Sorra tae Chorazim, an sorra tae Bethsaida, fer ïf tha fowk o Tyre an Sidon haed saen tha warkin o God's pooer as yous hae saen ït, the' wud hae repentit lang syne, an sut doon ïn seckclaith an eshes.  Hooaniver, tha fowk o Tyre an Sidon wull be bettèr aff on tha Day o Reckonin than yous wull.  An Capernaum, you micht thïnk ye'r weel on yer wye tae heiven. Na, but A'm tellin ye, ye'll be brocht doon tae hell.” Then he saed tae hïs follaers, “Whaiver lïstens tae yous ïs lïstenin tae me, an whaiver turns hïs bak on you, turns hïs bak on me; an whaiver turns hïs bak on me, turns hïs bak on tha Yin that sent me.” Whan tha seiventie cum bak, the' wur hairt gled an toul Jesus, “Loard, even tha ïll spïrits haed tae dae whut we bïd thaim ïn yer name!”  An he saed tae thaim, “A saa Satan faain frae heiven laik a flesh o lichtnin.  Luk noo, A hae gien yis tha thortie tae thramp on snakes an scorpions an tae owercum tha pooer o Satan, yer enemie. Thair's naethin wull be able tae dae yis onie hairm.  Nanethaless, haein pooer ower ïll spïrits ïs no tha thïng tae be gled aboot, but rether be gled that yer names ïs writ doon ïn heiven.” An thair an then Jesus wus owercum wi tha joy o tha Halie Spïrit, an he caad oot, “Faither, Loard o heiven an irth, A praise ye that ye hae kep these thïngs frae clivir an warlie-wise fowk, an made thaim clear eneuch fer weans tae unnèrstan. Ay, Faither, ït haes plaised ye tae dae ït thïs wye.  Ma Faither haes gien aa thïngs ower tae me, an naebodie kens wha tha Sinn raelie ïs apairt frae tha Faither, an naebodie fu kens tha Faither apairt frae tha Sinn, an whaiver tha Sinn wants tae reveal hïm tae.” An whan Jesus wus on hïs ain wi hïs follaers, he turnt tae thaim an saed, “Blisst ir tha een that see whut ye see.  A'll tell ye thïs, thair's monie proaphits an kïngs wud hae laikt tae see whut yous see, an the' dïdnae see ït; an tae hear whut yous hear, but the' dïdnae hear ït.” Yin day a thortie on tha Laa stud up an axt Jesus a question tae pit hïm tae tha test: “Maistèr, whut can A dae tae be shair A'll hae iverlastin life?”  An Jesus saed bak tae hïm, “Whut daes tha Laa o Moses say? Whut's yer unnèrstannin o ït?”  He answert an saed, “Ye maun love tha Loard yer God wi aa yer hairt, an yer sowl, an yer mine, micht an main; an yer nighber jist as much as yersel.”  An Jesus saed tae hïm, “Ay, that's tha richt answer. Dae thïs an ye'll leeve.” But he wantit tae keep hissel aheid o tha argyment, an he saed tae Jesus, “Ay, but wha ïs ma nighber?”  An Jesus saed, “Yin time thair wus thïs man trevelin frae Jerusalem tae Jericho an he wus set upon bi robbers, that strïpt hïm o hïs claes an gien hïm a richt hemmerin an left hïm half deid.  An bi chaunce a preesht cum alang, an whan he saen hïm he slipt bye on tha ither side o tha róad.  An eftèr thïs a Levite  cum bye. He stapt an lukt at tha man, an gaed bye on tha ither side as weel.  Then a Samaritan treveler cum tae whar he wus, an whan he saen hïm, hïs hairt went oot tae hïm.  An he went ower tae hïm an rowlt up hïs sairs, poorin on oyle an wine tae aise thaim, an sut hïm on hïs ain baist an brocht hïm tae an ïnn an lukt eftèr hïm.  Tha nixt moarnin, whan he wus leain, he tuk oot twa siller coins an gien thaim tae tha ïnnkeeper an saed, ‘Tak guid care o hïm an ïf ye ir oot o poaket, A'll mak ït up tae ye whan A cum bak.’ ”  Saed Jesus, “Noo, whutch o these thrie wus nighber tae tha bodie that got tha hemmerin frae tha robbers?”  An tha laayer saed, “Tha yin that tuk peetie on hïm.” Then Jesus saed, “You gang awa an dae tha same.” As Jesus an hïs follaers waakit on, the' cum tae a vïllage an a wumman caad Mairtha walcumed hïm ïntae hir hame.  She haed a sïstèr, Mary, that settelt hirsel doon at hïs feet an hung on iverie wurd he haed tae say.  But Mairtha wus aa o a floostèr ower aa that needit tae be daen, an she saed, “Loard, can ye no see ma sïstèr haes lef me tae dae aa tha wark, tell hir tae cum an gie iz a han.”  An Jesus answert, “Och Mairtha, ye ir gettin yersel aa warkt up aboot a hale lock o thïngs ye see need daen,  but onlie yin thïng raelie mettèrs. Mary haes waaled whut's best, an ït'll no be taen awa frae hir.” Yinst, whan Jesus wus oot prayin, yin o hïs follaers saed tae hïm, eftèr he haed quït, “Loard, lairn iz hoo tae pray, jist tha wye Jhone dïd wi hïs follaers.”  An he saed tae thaim, “Whan ye pray, say: ‘[Oor] Faither [that bides Abain], Halie be yer name. Micht yer Kïngdom cum shuin, [An yer wull be daen on irth, jist tha wye ït ïs Abain.] Gie iz theday eneuch breid tae dae iz. An forgie iz oor wrangdaeins, laik we forgie thaim that daes wrang agin us. An dïnnae róad iz ïntae temptation, [but save iz frae aa ïll .]’ ” Then Jesus saed tae thaim, “Sayin ye went tae a freen's hoose ïn tha mïddle o tha nicht an saed tae hïm, ‘Cud A borra thrie loafs o breid, acause a freen o mine haes cum tae vïsit an thair's nae mait ïn tha hoose’. An sayin tha freen caas oot, ‘Dïnnae bother me, tha dure's lockt an me an tha weans ïs ïn bed. A'm no gettin up tae gie ye oniethin!’  Even he daesnae get up an gie hïm whut he's lukkin, ïf ye keep on knockin lang eneuch, he'll rise an gie hïm aa he needs.  An A say: Keep on axin, an ït wull be gien tae ye, keep on lukkin an ye'll fin whut ye'r eftèr, keep on rappin an tha dure wull be apent tae ye.  Fer iveriebodie that axes wull get; hïm that keeps on lukkin wull fin whut he's eftèr; an tae hïm that keeps on rappin, tha dure wull be apent.  If a sinn axes breid frae onie o yis that's a faither, wull he gie hïm a stane; or ïf he axes a fïsh wull he gie hïm a snake?  Or ïf he axes an egg wud he offer hïm a scorpion?  An sae ïf sïnfu fowk laik yersels know hoo tae gie guid thïngs tae yer weans, hoo much mair wull yer heivenlie Faither gie tha Halie Spïrit tae thaim that axes hïm!” Yinst, Jesus wus castin oot a dum spïrit frae a man. An whaniver tha demon left hïm an tha man that wus dum stairtit tae taak, tha fowk wur dumfoonèrt.  But some o thaim saed, “He casts demons oot throu tha pooer o Beelzebul, tha heidyin o tha demons.”  But ithers tried tae ketch hïm oot bi axin fer a sign frae heiven.  An Jesus, knowin' whut wus ïn thair mines, saed, “A kïngdom divïd agin ïtsel wull gae tae reck an ruin, an a hoose divïd agin ïtsel wull faa doon.  Sae ïf Satan ïs divïd agin hissel, hïs kïngdom cudnae stan, cud ït? Hoo then can ye say that A cast oot demons throu tha pooer o Beelzebul?  If yis say that A cast oot ïll spïrits bi tha pooer o Beelzebul, bi whut pooer then daes yer ain fowk cast thaim oot? Sae let thaim be tha yins tae judge ye fer whut ye hae saed.  But ïf A, wi tha fïng'r o God cast oot ïll spïrits, ït proves that tha Kïngdom o God ïs here amang ye.  Whaniver a strang man that's weel-airmed gairds hïs castle, hïs belangins ïs safe.  But whaniver a strang'r man attecks an gets tha bettèr o hïm, he taks awa aa tha armour he lippens on, an tha belangins ïs aa divïd oot.  Hïm that's no for me ïs agin me; an hïm that ïsnae giein me a han tae gether ïn, he micht as weel be scattèrin. Whan an ïll spïrit cums oot o a man, ït raiks throu tha desert lukkin fer rest, an whan ït daesnae fin onie, ït says, ‘A'll jist gae bak tae whar A wus leevin afore.’ Sae tha spïrit gaes bak tae tha hoose ït left an fins ït swep clain an aa redd up. Then ït luks fer seiven ither spïrits mair wïckit ner ïtsel, an the' aa gae ïn an settle thair. An that man enns up faur waur ner he wus afore.” An while Jesus wus taakin, a wumman ïn tha getherin caad oot, “Blisst ïs tha wumman that gien ye birth an nurst ye as a wean!”  An he saed bak tae hir, “But mair blisst ir tha yins that hear tha wurd o God an heed ït!” Mair an mair fowk wus jundyin roon hïm, an he begun tae praich tae thaim sayin, “We'r leevin ïn evil times wi evil fowk. The' keep lukkin fer a sign, but nane wull be gien thaim, apairt frae tha sign o Jonah, tha proaphit.  Fer jist as Jonah wus a sign tae tha Ninevites, ïn tha same wye A, tha Sinn o Man, wull be a sign tae thïs genèration.  Tha Queen o tha Sooth wull stan up on Judgemen Day wi tha men o thïs genèration an she wull condemn thaim, fer she cum frae tha enns o tha irth fer tae lïsten tae Solomon's wusdom. Yit yin abain Solomon ïs here noo, an the'ir no lïstenin!  Tha men o Nineveh wull stan up ïn that Day as weel wi thïs genèration, an the'll condemn ït; fer they repentit whaniver Jonah praicht tae thaim, an yit yin abain Jonah ïs here noo. Naebodie lichts a lamp an pits ït unnèr a boul fer tae hide ïts licht, but the' pit ït up on a stan whar aa can see ïts licht.  Yer ee ïs tha lamp o yer bodie, an ïf yer ee ïs guid, yer hale bodie ïs fu o licht; but whan yer ee ïs baad, yer hale bodie's fu o dairkness.  Noo tha licht ye thïnk ye hae, tak heed that ït's no dairkness.  An sae ïf ye be aa fu o licht wi nae wee dairk coarners, yer hale bodie wull be glowin, laik whan a bricht licht shines on ye.” An while he wus taakin, a Pharisee axt hïm tae hïs hoose fer a bite tae ait, an he went ïn an sut doon.  Tha Pharisee got a gunk whan he saa that Jesus dïdnae waash afore dennèr.  But tha Loard saed tae hïm, “Yous Pharisees waash tha ootside o tha bickers an plates, but inside ye'r fu o greed an wïckitness.  Ye coofs, hae ye no tha sense tae know that God made tha inside as weel as tha ootside?  Gie tae tha puir oot o whut ye hae on yer ain plate, an then ye'll be clain throu an throu. Lïsten here, wae faa ye, Pharisees, ye gie a tenth o yer gairden spices sitch as mint an rue, but ye hae neglectit justice, an ye dïnnae love God. But ye shudnae ferget tae be fair an kine tae ithers, an tae love God, as weel as giein yer tenth.  Wae faa ye, Pharisees, fer ye aye laik tae hae tha best saits ïn tha Meetin Hooses, aye wantin fowk tae touch thair keps tae ye ïn tha mairket places.  Ay, wae faa ye, [Pharisees, maistèrs o tha Laa an hippycrates], fer yis ir laik graves wi nae mairkins that men waak ower wi'oot knowin.” Then yin o tha laayers saed tae Jesus, “Maistèr, ir ye gettin at us as weel?”  He saed, “Ye'r ïn fer bother tae, yous laayers, fer yis gie men burdens ower wechtie tae cairt, an ye dïnnae lïft a fïng'r yersels tae gie a han.  Wae faa ye, fer yis big fancie monuments on tha graves o tha verie proaphits that yer faithers kïllt lang syne.  Yer faithers kïllt thaim but yous bigged tha monuments, sae ye maun gae alang wi whut the' daen.  God, then, ïn hïs wusdom saed, ‘A wull senn thaim proaphits an possels. The' wull kïll a wheen o thaim an gie tha rest a haird time.’  Sae tha bluid o aa tha proaphits spïllt frae tha begïnnin o tha warl, yous fowk leevin noo hae ït on yer heids -  frae tha kïllin o Abel tae tha kïllin o Zechariah atween tha althar an tha Hoose o God. Ay, A'm tellin yis, yous'll pye fer thïs!  Ay, ye'r ïn fer bother tae, yous laayers, fer yis hae taen awa tha key tae unnèrstannin. Yis hinnae uised ït yersels, an yis hae kep ither fowk frae uisin ït as weel.” Whaniver Jesus quït taakin, tha Pharisees an tha maistèrs o tha Laa wus wile ang'rie an heckelt hïm,  tryin tae get hïm tae cum oot wi sumthin that the' cud fin faut wi, fer tae get hïm arrestit. Mainwhile thoosans o fowk gethert up sae thrang that the' wur thrampin yin anither. Jesus spauk furst o aa tae hïs follaers an toul thaim, “Be on yer gaird agin tha yeast o tha Pharisees, fer the' let on tae be guid an the'r faur frae ït!  Thair's naethin covert ower that'll no cum tae licht, ner hïd that'll no be kent.  Sae, whutiver's taakt aboot ïn tha dairk wull be heerd ïn tha braid daylicht, an whut ye hae whuspert aboot behin shut dures wull be blared oot frae tha ruiftaps. Lïsten freens, dïnnae be feart o thaim that kïll tha bodie, fer eftèr that thair's naethin mair the' can dae.  But A'll warn ye noo wha ye shud fear. Fear hïm that haes tha pooer tae kïll, an then tae throw ïntae hell. Ay, A tell ye, fear hïm!  Shair five wee sparras ir soul fer a wheen o happence, ir the' no? An God daesnae ferget onie o thaim.  But even tha verie hairs o yer heid ir aa coontit, sae dïnnae be feart, yis ir warth mair ner a hale wheen o sparras. An A'm tellin ye, whaiver's no feart tae tell fowk the' belang tae me, tha Sinn o Man wull own hïm tae afore tha angels o God.  But oniebodie that daesnae admït tae bein a follaer o mine, wull be denied bi me afore tha angels o God.  An whaiver spakes a wurd agin tha Sinn o Man wull be forgien, but whaiver spakes ïll agin tha Halie Spïrit wull no be forgien.  Whan yis ir brocht afore tha Meetin Hoose offyshals an heidyins, dïnnae be ower enxious aboot yer answer or whut tae say,  fer tha Halie Spïrit wull pit tha wurds ïn yer mooth whan tha time cums.” An yin o tha crood saed tae hïm, “Maistèr, wud ye hae a wurd wi ma brither, an ax hïm tae share wi me whut wus lef tae iz?”  An he saed tae hïm, “Freen, wha gien me tha richt tae settle a dïffernce atween you an yer brither?”  An Jesus saed tae thaim, “Tak heed that yis ir no aye wantin thïngs that ither fowk hae, fer a man's life ïs no jist a mettèr o whut he gethers aboot hïm.” An he toul thaim thïs parable, “Yin time, a weel tae dae fairmer haed a guid hairst.  An he swuthered aboot whut he wus gaun tae dae, fer he haed nae ruim tae store ït aa.  Sae he saed tae hissel, ‘A ken whut A'll dae, A'll tummle ma barns an big yins that'll houl aa ma grain an guids.  An A'll say tae masel: A hae plentie lef bye me tae dae me fer monie a yeir, sae A'll jist ait, drïnk an hae a guid time tae masel.’  But God saed, ‘Ye ir a fool, fer ye'll be caad awa thïs verie nicht, an wha'll get aa tha stuff ye hae lef behin?’  In tha same wye tha man's a fool that gethers up stuff fer hissel, an haesnae stored up tha richt soart o treysure wi God.” An Jesus turnt tae hïs follaers an saed, “A'm tellin ye, yis ir tae tak nae thocht fer yer life or yer bodie, whut tae ait or whut tae pit on ye.  Thair's mair tae life ner mait an claes.  Luk at tha craws, the' nether sow ner reap an hae nae barns tae store oniethin ïn, yit the' get eneuch tae dae thaim, fer God feeds thaim. Ir yous no warth mair tae hïm than a wheen o burds?  Ye cannae add an oor tae yer life bi worryin aboot ït,  sae, ïf ye cannae dae a wee thïng laik that, why worrie yersel aboot oniethin else?  Noo, tak tha lïlies, ye see hoo the' growe; the' dïnnae wark an the' dïnnae spïn, yit A'll tell ye thïs, e'en Solomon, wi aa hïs fancie claes, cudnae match thaim!  An ïf God pits claes on tha gress ïn tha fiel that's here theday an throwed ïntae tha fire themorra, dae you dooters no unnèrstan that he'll luk eftèr you anaa?.  Sae dïnnae worrie aboot mait or drïnk. Dïnnae bother yer heids aboot ït.  It's thaim at daesnae know God that rin eftèr sitch thïngs, but yer Faither abain kens whut ye hae need o.  But yous ir tae seek oot hïs Kïngdom, an tha ither thïngs wull tak care o thairsels. Dïnnae be scarred, wee flock, fer yer faither wants tae gie ye tha Kïngdom.  Sell aff whut ye hae an gie tha siller tae tha puir, an thïs wull coont as treysure stored up ïn strang safe moneybaags ïn heiven, whar ït'll nether be stole bi thiefs ner et wi moths.  Fer whut yis thïnk tha maist o, wull aye be ïn yer hairt. Be aa dresst up an readie wi tha hoose lït up; ect laik men waitin on thair maistèr tae cum bak frae tha waddin, sae that whan he knocks yis can apen tha dure tae hïm richt awa.  Whaniver tha maistèr cums, blisst ir tha yins he fins watchin an waitin. A tell yis thïs, he'll get hissel readie, sït thaim doon, an he hissel wull sarve thaim, an lea tha mait oot afore thaim.  Tha maistèr wull mebbe cum bak ïn tha wee smaa oors, or at tha scraich o day, but ïf he fins thaim readie an waitin whaniver he cums, the' wull be blisst aa richt!  Ye can be shair o thïs: ïf ye haed a hoose, an ye knowed tha day an oor a thief wus cumin, ye'd be lukkin oot fer hïm, wud ye no? Ye wudnae alloo yer hoose tae be brauk ïntae.  Sae yous maun be readie, fer ye dïnnae ken tha oor tha Sinn o Man wull cum.” Then Petèr saed, “Loard, dïd ye main these thïngs fer iveriebodie, or jist fer us?”  An tha Loard saed, “A'm taakin tae onie wise an faithfu sarvint, whase maistèr ïs able tae lea hïm ïn chairge o tha ither sarvints ïn hïs hoose, tae gie iveriebodie thair fair share o mait at tha richt time.  Onie sarvint ectin laik thïs whaniver hïs maistèr cums bak, wull be a happie man.  A'll tell ye thïs, he'll pit that sarvint ïn chairge o iveriethin he haes.  But ïf tha sarvint says tae hissel, ‘He's a lang time o cumin, tha maistèr’, an he aits an gets drunk an he stairts tae bate up aa tha ither sarvints - weel noo, tha maistèr wull cum bak on a day an oor whan he's no lukkin oot fer hïm, an tha maistèr wull dae awa wi that sarvint. He wull trait hïm jist laik an unbeliever.  An that sarvint that knowed richtlie whut tae dae, an dïdnae dae whut he wus toul bi tha maistèr an mak readie, he'll get yin guid whalin.  But tha yin that dïd wrang whaniver he dïdnae unnèrstan whut he shud a daen, he'll get aff aisie, tha mair he daesnae desarve ït. God wull ax a lock frae thaim that's bin gien a lock. Tha mair the' hae bin gien tae luk eftèr, tha mair the' wull hae tae answer fer. A'm cum tae kïnnel a fire on irth, an A wush ït wus aareadie lït!  A hae a tarrible baptisin aheid o me, an awfu testin tae ït's aa ower.  Dae ye thïnk A cum tae brïng peace on irth? Deed na, ït's deveesion A brïng.  Frae noo a hoose wi five fowk wull be divïd, wi thrie agin twa an twa agin thrie.  Tha faither wull be divïd agin tha sinn, an tha sinn agin tha faither; tha mither agin tha dochtèr an tha dochtèr agin tha mither; tha mither-ïn-laa agin tha dochtèr-ïn-laa; an tha dochtèr-ïn-laa agin tha mither-ïn-laa.” An Jesus saed tae tha crood o fowk, “Whaniver ye see cloods cumin ïn frae tha Wast, ye ken we'r fer haein rain, an, richt eneuch, doon ït cums!  An whan tha wun blaas frae tha Sooth, ye ken we'r ïn fer a scorcher, an sae ït ïs.  Yous hippycrates, yis can read tha luk o tha sky aa richt, but yis cannae see tha signs aa roon aboot ye o whut's tae cum. Why dae yis no see fer yersels whut's richt?  If oniebodie pits tha blame on ye an taks ye tae coort, ye shud dae yer best tae settle tha mettèr oot o coort. If ye dïnnae, then ye'll be up afore tha judge an he'll turn ye ower tae tha offysher, an ye'll enn up ïn jail.  Fer ïf that's tha wye ït enns up, ye'll no git oot o thair afore yer last pennie's pyed!” At that parteeclar time, Jesus wus toul that Pilate haed kïllt some fowk frae Galilee while the' wur offerin secryfices ïn tha Hoose o tha Loard.  He saed tae thaim, “Dae ye jalouse tha yins that suffert laik thïs haed daen mair wrang ner aa tha ither Galileeans?  Na, A tell ye thïs, ïf yis dïnnae repent, tha hale lock o yis'll perish as weel.  Or whut aboot tha echteen that deed ïn Siloam whaniver tha tooer cum doon on tap o thaim? Dae ye jalouse that thair wrangdaeins wus waur ner aa tha ither yins ïn Jerusalem?  Na, A tell ye thïs, ïf yis dïnnae repent, tha hale lock o ye wull perish forbye.” Then Jesus toul thaim a parable. “Thair wus thïs man haed a fïg tree plantit ïn hïs vineyaird. Yin day, he cum tae ït tae see ïf thair wus onie fruit on ït, but he fun nane.  Sae he saed tae tha gairdner, ‘Luk here, thïs thrie yeir A hae cum lukkin fer fïgs on thïs tree, an thair's nane on ït! Cut ït doon! It's a waste o guid grun.’  Tha gairdner saed, ‘Lea ït alane, sïr, gie ït anither yeir. A'll dïg roon ït an gie ït a guid dressin o dung.  If thair's onie fïgs on ït nixt yeir, weel an guid, an ïf no, we'll cut ït doon fer ye.’ ” Noo, yin Sabbath day, whan Jesus wus taichin ïn yin o tha Meetin Hooses,  thair wus a wumman that haed bin baad fer echteen yeir acause o an ïll spïrit. She wus bent dooble an cudnae stan up strecht ava.  Whan Jesus saa hir, he caad hir an saed tae hir, “Wumman, ye'r redd o yer seeckness, an ye'r noo free!”  An he püt hïs hans on hir, an she stud up hir fu heicht, an gien praise tae God.  But tha heidyin o tha Meetin Hoose wus ang'rie, acause Jesus haed hailt tha wumman on tha Sabbath day, an he saed tae tha fowk, “Ye hae sïx days tae dae aa yer wark. Cum tae be hailt on yin o thaim days an no on tha Sabbath!”  An thïs ïs hoo tha Loard answert hïm. “Yis oul hippycrates! Shair, dae yis no lowse yer kye an yer cuddies frae tha staal on tha Sabbath, an tak thaim oot tae wattèr thaim?  Wus ït no richt that on tha Sabbath A shud set free thïs wumman o tha femlie o Abraham, that haes bin hel ïn bondage bi Satan thïs echteen yeir?”  Thïs püt hïs enemies tae shame, tha hale lock o thaim; an aa tha fowk wus hairt gled at aa tha wunnèrfu thïngs he daen. Then Jesus saed, “Fer whut laik ïs tha Kïngdom o God? Wha shud A compare ït wi?  It ïs laik a wee mustèrt seed that a bodie tuk an plantit ïn hïs gairden an ït growed ïntae a tree, a tree bïg eneuch fer wee burds tae tak shiltèr ïn ïts brenches.” An he saed agane, “Fer whut laik ïs tha Kïngdom o God? Whut shud A compare ït wi?  It's laik a wee taste o yeast that a wumman pits ïn a bïg boul o flure. An ït spreeds aa throu ït, tae tha hale lock o ït ïs ris.” An he gaed throu tha toons an vïllages, taichin as he went, aye heidin on nixt Jerusalem.  An summodie axt hïm, “Wull thair jist be a wheen o fowk saved, Loard?” An he saed tae thaim aa,  “Dae aa ye can tae get ïn bi tha nerra dure. Fer monies a yin wull try an get ïn, an no be fït tae.  Fer yinst tha Heid o tha Hoose haes got up an lockt tha dure, ye'll be stannin ootbye rappin an caain oot, ‘Sïr, wull ye no apen tha dure tae iz?’ An he'll cum bak wi, ‘A'm tellin ye, A know naethin aboot ye, or whar yis cum frae!’  Then ye'll say, ‘But we et an drunk alang wi ye, an ye hae taicht iz doon oor loanins.’  But he'll cum bak wi, ‘A tell ye, A dïnnae know a thïng aboot ye, or whar ye cum frae. Ye rapscallions ye! Git oot o ma sicht, tha hale lock o yis!’  Thair'll be greetin an scringein o teeth whaniver ye see Abraham an Isaac an Jacob an aa tha proaphits ïn tha Kïngdom o God, an yous aa shut oot.  An fowk wull cum frae aa airts an tak thair place roon tha boord ïn tha Kïngdom o God.  But tak heed, thair's yins that's last that'll be furst, an thair's ither yins that's furst that'll be last.” Jist then some Pharisees cum up an saed tae hïm, “Get oot o here ïf ye want tae leeve, fer Herod haes ït ïn mine tae kïll ye!”  “Gang tell thon sleekit oul fox,” saed Jesus tae thaim, “that ‘A'll be keepin on castin oot ïll spïrits an hailin tha seeck theday an themorra. An tha day eftèr that A'll hae daen whut A wus sent tae dae.’  Nanethaless, theday, themorra an tha nixt day, A maun gang on ma róad, fer ït wudnae dae fer a proaphit o God tae dee ootside o Jerusalem.  O Jerusalem, Jerusalem, ye kïll tha proaphits an stane thaim that's sent tae ye! Monies tha time A wantit tae gether yer weans thegither, laik a hen gethers hir lachter o wee burds unnèr hir wïngs, but yis wudnae let me!  Luk, yer Hoose ïs empie noo. But A tell ye thïs, yis'll no see me agane til ye say, ‘Blisst ïs tha Yin that cums ïn tha name o tha Loard’!” Yin Sabbath day, Jesus went fer a bite tae ait at tha hoose o yin o tha heidyins o tha Pharisees, an the' wur aa keepin thair ee on hïm.  An fornent hïm wus thïs man wi hïs bodie aa swallt up.  Sae Jesus axt tha laayers an Pharisees, “Daes tha Laa alloo ye tae hail fowk on tha Sabbath day, or no?”  The' haed nae answer tae that. Sae he layed hïs han on tha man, an he hailt hïm an sent hïm awa.  An he turnt tae thaim an saed, “Jist say, yin o yis haed a cuddie  or a coo that faad doon ïntil a wal, wud ye no gae an pu ït oot strecht aff, Sabbath day or no?”  The' cudnae gie hïm onie answer tae that ava. Whan Jesus saa tha fowk thair aa makkin fer tha best saits ïn tha hoose, he toul thaim thïs parable:  “Whaniver ye get an ïnvite tae a waddin, dïnnae be settin yersel doon at tha tap table, fer anither bodie mair impoartin ner yersel micht be cumin tae ït.  Sae then tha yin that axt baith o yis tae tha waddin wud hae tae say tae ye, ‘Wull ye gie thïs man yer sait?’ Ye wudnae know whar tae pit yersel, wud ye? An ye'll hae tae shïft tae tha bak o tha ruim!  But whan ye get an ïnvite, gang an sït doon at tha bak, an whan tha yin that ïnvitit ye sees ye, he wull say, ‘Freen, whut ir ye daein awa bak thair? Cum on up here tae tha front!’ Then aa tha ither fowk thair wull see that ye ir summodie!  Whaiver sets hissel up as summodie, tha Loard'll brïng hïm doon. Whaiver taks tha hummle place, wull be gien tha place o honour.” Then Jesus turnt tae tha yin that haed gien hïm tha ïnvite an saed, “Whan ye gie a dennèr or a pairtie, dïnnae be caain yer freens, or yer brithers, yer femlie or yer weel-aff nighbers, acause the' wull onlie pye ye bak bi ïnvitin ye ïn return.  But whan ye gie a bïg swaree, caa aa tha puir, tha lameters, tha halt an tha blin fowk.  The' cannae pye ye bak, but God wull bliss ye an gie ye yer reward whan he rises tha upricht fowk frae tha deid.” Whan yin o thaim that wus sïttin at table wi Jesus heerd thïs, he saed tae hïm, “Blisst ïs tha yin that wull sït doon tae ait ïn tha Kïngdom o God.”  Then Jesus saed tae hïm, “Yinst thair wus thïs man giein a bïg pairtie, an he axt a hale lock o fowk tae ït.  An whan tha time fer tha bïg pairtie cum roon, he sent hïs sarvin man oot wi a message fer tha yins that wus axt: ‘Ye ir tae cum noo, fer iveriethin's readie.’  But the' stairtit yin an aa tae mak excuses. Tha furst yin saed, ‘A hae jist bocht a bït o lan, an A hae tae gang an luk at ït. A beg ye tae let me aff.’  Anither yin saed, ‘A hae bocht five yauk o kye, an A hae tae gang an try thaim oot. A beg ye tae let me aff.’  An anither saed, ‘Luk, A hae jist got merriet! A cannae cum.’ ”  “Sae,” saed Jesus, “tha sarvin man cum an gien an accoont o ït tae hïs maistèr. Then tha maistèr o tha hoose wus wile ang'rie, an he toul hïs sarvin man, ‘Gang oot quïck ïntae tha raas an tha entries, an brïng ïn tha puir, tha lameters, tha blin an tha halt fowk.’  Latèr on, tha sarvin man cum bak an saed, ‘Maistèr, A hae daen as ye bïd me, yit thair's still ruim fer mair.’  An tha maistèr toul hïs sarvin man, ‘Gang oot ïntae tha róads an loanins; dïnnae tak Na fer an answer, mak thaim cum, fer A want ma hoose fïllt! An A'll tell yis thïs’, qo he, ‘nane o thaim that wur ïnvitit at tha furst wull iver sup wi me!’ ” Bïg croods wus follaein Jesus, an he turnt tae thaim an saed,  “If onie man cums tae me, an pits hïs faither or hïs mither, hïs wife or hïs weans, hïs brithers or sïstèrs, ay, or even hïs ain sel afore me, he cannae be ma follaer.  Whaiver daesnae tak up hïs ain cross, an cum eftèr me, cannae be a follaer o mine. Jist say yin o yis haes a mine tae big a tooer. Wud he no sït doon furst an coont tha coast, tae see ïf he haes eneuch tae feenish ït?  Eftèr he haes püt ïn tha fïttins, ïf he fins he's no able tae feenish ït - aa tha fowk roon aboot wull mak fun o hïm, wull the' no?  The' wull say, ‘Thïs man stairtit tae big, an wusnae able tae feenish tha jab!’ Or agane, ïf a kïng wus gaun tae war wi anither kïng, wud he no sït doon furst an jalouse ïf he wud be able, wi ten thoosan sodgers, tae bate hïm that's cumin agin hïm wi twuntie thoosan?  If he fins he's no able, then while hïs enemie ïs a lang róad aff, he'll senn a go-between tae hïm, an ax fer terms o peace.  Jist ïn tha same wye, whaiver o yis wull no gie up aa ye hae, cannae be ma follaer. Saut ïs guid; but ïf ït loasses ïts taste, hoo dae ye mak ït saltie agane?  It ïs nether fït fer tha lan ner tha midden; fowk jist clod ït oot. Let hïm that haes ears ïn hïs heid tak tent!” Noo tha tex men an tha wrangdaers gethert roon tae gie hïm thair ear.  An tha Pharisees an tha maistèrs o tha Laa kep grummlin an the' saed, “Thïs man ïs weel ïn wi wrangdaers an e'en gaes ïn fer a bite tae ait wi thaim.” Sae Jesus toul thaim thïs parable an he saed,  “Say a man amang yis haed a hunnèr sheep; ïf he loast yin o thaim, wud he no lea tha ninetie-nine oot on tha muirs, an gang eftèr tha yin that wus loast til he fins ït?  An whan he haes fun ït, he's gye gled an he pits ït on hïs shoodèr, an he heids awa hame wi ït.  An whan he gets hame, he caas thegither hïs freens an nighbers an he says tae thaim, ‘Cum on an see. Ir yis no hairt gled wi me A hae fun ma loast sheep?’  A tell yis, jist ïn tha same wye, thair wull be mair joy ïn heiven ower yin wrangdaer that repents o hïs wrangdaein, mair ner ower ninetie-nine that thïnks the' dïnnae need tae repent.” “Or agane, ïf a wumman haed ten siller coins an she loast yin o thaim, wud she no tak a bricht licht, redd up tha hoose, an luk ïn iverie neuk an crannie tae she fins ït?  An whaniver she's fun ït, she caas thegither hir freens an nighbers an she says, ‘Cum on an see. Ir yis no hairt gled wi me A hae fun ma loast coin?’  A tell yis, jist ïn tha same wye, thair's joy amang tha angels o God ower yin wrangdaer that turns frae hïs wrangdaein.” Jesus went on tae say, “Thair wus thïs man wi twa sinns.  Tha young'r yin saed tae hïs faither, ‘Can A hae noo whut ye wur fer leain me ïn yer wull?’ Sae tha faither divïd whut he haed atween tha twa o thaim.  A wheen o days latèr, tha young'r yin gethert up aa hïs belangins an he went aff tae a faur-aff kintrie. He spent aa roon hïm ïn wile leevin.  Aboot tha time hïs money run oot, thair wus a wile baad famine ower tha hale lan, an he wus starvin wi hung'r.  Sae he hired hissel oot tae a local fairmer that sent hïm oot tae hïs fiels tae feed pïgs.  Tha young fella wus that hung'rie got, he wus near aitin tha husks he wus feedin tae tha pïgs. An naebodie gien hïm ocht ava.  Whan he cum tae hïs senses he thocht tae hissel, ‘Ma faither's sarvints bak hame haes eneuch tae ait an tae spare, an here A am, deein wi hung'r!  A'll git up an A'll gae hame tae ma faither an A'll say: A hae sïnned agin heiven an agin yersel,  an A'm nae lang'r fït tae be caad yer sinn. Wud ye no tak me on as yin o yer hired hans?’  Sae he ris up an he went bak hame tae hïs faither. But whan he wus yit a lang róads aff, hïs faither saa hïm cumin, an hïs hairt went oot tae hïm, an he run an throwed hïs airms roon hïm an he kïsst hïm.  Tha sinn saed tae hïm, ‘A hae sïnned agin heiven an agin yersel, an A'm nae mair fït tae be caad yer sinn.’  But tha faither saed tae hïs sarvints, ‘Rin, brïng oot tha guid robe an pit ït on hïm, pit a rïng on hïs fïng'r an shune on hïs feet.  An brïng forrit tha kwye we wur fattenin up, an kïll ït, fer we'r gaun tae hae a bïg pairtie.  Fer thïs sinn o mine wus deid, an noo he's bak tae life agane; he wus loast, but noo he's fun.’ Sae tha pairtie begun. Noo while aa thïs wus gaun on, tha ouler sinn wus oot warkin ïn tha fiels, an whan he cum near tha hoose he heerd aa tha music an dauncin.  Sae he caad yin o tha sarvints an he axt hïm whut wus gaun on.  Tha sarvint toul hïm, ‘Yer brither haes cum hame, an yer faither haes kïllt tha wee kwye we wur fattenin, fer he's gled tae hae hïs sinn hame safe an siccar.’  Tha ouler brither wus rïppin an he wudnae gae ïntae tha hoose; sae hïs faither cum oot an tried tae taak hïm roon.  But he saed tae hïs faither, ‘Luk, A hae wrocht haird fer ye aa these yeirs, an no yinst hae A no daen yer bïddin. Aa thïs time ye niver even gien me a wee góat tae hae a swaree wi ma freens!  Yit whan thïs waster o a sinn o yers cums hame, eftèr skailin yer money aa roon hïm on baad weemen an tha laik, ye gae an kïll tha best kwye aboot tha place fer hïm!’  An tha faither saed, ‘Ma sinn, ye ir aye wi me, an aa that A hae ïs yours.  It's onlie but richt we shud be joyfu an gled, fer thïs brither o yers wus deid, an noo he's bak tae life. He wus loast, but noo he's fun.’ ” An Jesus went on tae say tae hïs follaers, “Yinst thair wus a weel-aff man that haed a bodie lukkin eftèr hïs affairs, an summodie toul hïm that thïs owerseer wus squannèrin iveriethin.  Sae tha weel-aff man confrontit hïm aboot thïs an he saed, ‘Whut's thïs A hear aboot ye? Gie an accoont o whut ye hae daen, fer A'll no hae ye aboot tha place onie mair.’  Then tha owerseer saed tae hissel, ‘Whut'll A dae whan A hae nae studie wark? A'm no fït tae dïg an A wud be affrontit tae beg.  A know whut A'll dae, sae that fowk dïnnae gie me tha coul shoodèr whaniver A loass ma jab!’  Yin bi yin he caad ïn tha fowk that wur ïn debt tae hïs boss, an he axt tha furst yin, ‘Hoo much dae ye owe tha maistèr?’  ‘A hunnèr barrels o oyle,’ saed he. Sae tha owerseer toul hïm, ‘Tak yer bïll, sït doon thair quïck an pit doon fïftie!’  An tae anither he saed, ‘An whut dae ye owe?’ ‘A hunnèr baags o wheat,’ saed he. Sae tha owerseer saed tae hïm, ‘Luk here, tak yer bïll an pit doon echtie baags!’  Tha maistèr o tha crookit owerseer haed tae gie credit tae hïm fer tha wye he haed o gettin ïn wi fowk. Fer tha fowk o thïs warl ir whiles mair lang-heidit ïn thair dailins than tha yins that hae saen tha licht.  An A'm tellin ye, yis shud uise yer warlie siller tae mak freens ïn tha warl; an sae, whan money's nae mair use tae ye, yis wull be gien a walcum ïntae yer iverlastin hame. If yis ir faithfu ïn wee thïngs then yis wull be faithfu ïn bïgger yins. In tha same wye, hïm that's no strecht ïn wee thïngs wull no be strecht ïn bïg thïngs.  If yis cannae be trustit wi warlie walth, wha wull trust yis wi tha true riches o heiven?  If ye cannae be trustit wi ither fowk's money, wha wull gie ye money o yer ain tae luk eftèr?  A slave cannae sarve twa maistèrs; fer ether he'll hait tha yin an love tha ither, or he'll stïck bye tha yin an thïnk naethin o tha ither. Ye cannae sarve baith God an Gowld.” An tha Pharisees that laikt thair money heerd aa thïs, an the' stairtit tae geg hïm.  But he saed tae thaim, “Yous ir tha yins that try tae prove yersels richt ïn tha sicht o fowk, but God knows whut's ïn yer hairts, fer tha thïngs that's tarrible weel thocht o bi men wud be a scunnèr tae God. Afore Jhone, fowk leeved bi tha Laa o Moses an tha proaphits; but noo tha Kïngdom o God ïs praicht, an iveriebodie's püshin thair wye ïn.  But that daesnae main that tha Laa daesnae stan, fer ït daes, ïn iverie wee point. It's as strang an studie as heiven an irth thegither. Whaiver pits awa hïs wife an gets merriet agane ïs commïttin adultèrie; an whaiver merries hir that's divorced commïts adultèrie as weel.” An Jesus went on tae say, “Yin time thair wus thïs weel-aff man that dresst up ïn fancie claes, an leeved iverie day ïn tha lap o luxurie.  An then thair wus thïs puir beggar, covert wi sairs, caad Lazarus, that lay at hïs gate.  Lazarus wus hopin that tha rich man wud gie hïm tha leains frae hïs table. Whiles, tha doags wud cum an lïck hïs sairs.  In tha enn tha beggar deed an tha angels cairriet hïm awa tae be wi Abraham. Tha rich man deed forbye an wus buriet.  An whan he wus sufferin sair ïn hell he cud see Abraham an Lazarus thegither a lang wyes aff.  An he cryed oot tae thaim an saed, ‘Faither Abraham, tak peetie on me an senn Lazarus tae dook tha enn o hïs fïng'r ïn tha wattèr tae cool ma tung doon, fer A'm tormentit wi tha bleeze o thïs fire!’  But Abraham saed, ‘Ma sinn, dae ye mine tha time whan ye wur leevin on irth? You haed iveriethin an Lazarus haed naethin, an noo he's at peace an ye ir tormentit.  An apairt frae aa that, thair's a bïg deep sheuch atween iz baith, sae that we can hae nae dailins wi yin anither.’  Then tha rich man saed, ‘Faither Abraham, wud ye no senn Lazarus tae ma faither's hoose tae warn ma five brithers, sae that the' dïnnae enn up here ïn torment laik masel?’  But Abraham saed bak tae hïm, ‘The' hae bin aareadie warnt bi Moses an tha proaphits - let thaim tak heed tae that warnin!’  An tha rich man saed, ‘Na, faither Abraham, but ïf summodie frae tha deid appeart tae thaim, the' wud turn awa frae thair sïns an bak tae God.’  But Abraham saed, ‘If the' dïnnae heed whut Moses an tha proaphits toul thaim, then ït'll no mak onie dïffernce ïf summodie cum bak tae thaim frae tha deid.’ ” Yin day Jesus saed tae hïs follaers, “Thair'll aye be temptation tae dae wrang, but dear halp tha yin that daes tha tempin!  It wud be faur bettèr fer hïm ïf a mïllstane wus hung roon hïs neck an he wus drapt ïntae tha sea, rether ner hïm leadin yin o these puir wee craitèrs asthray.  Lïsten here, ïf summodie daes ocht agin ye, tell hïm he shudnae hae daen ït, an ïf he says he's sorrie, then forgie hïm.  An ïf he keeps on daein ye wrang seiven times a day an ïs sorrie iverie time, then ye maun still forgie hïm.” An tha possels saed tae tha Loard, “Show iz hoo we can hae mair faith.”  An tha Loard saed, “If yis haed faith as smaa as a mustèrt seed even, yis cud say tae thïs mulberry tree, ‘Cum oot bi tha ruit an plant yersel ïn tha sea’, an richt awa ït'd dae whut ït's toul. Whaniver yer sarvin man cums ïn frae tha plooin an mindin tha beese, ye wudnae say tae hïm, ‘Sït yersel doon quïck an hae a bite tae ait.’ Rether ye wud tell hïm tae clain hissel up an sarve you furst, an then tak hïs ain eftèr.  A doot ye wudnae say, ‘Thenks’, tae yer ain man fer daein whut he's pyed tae dae!  In tha same wye, whan ye dae ma bïddin, ye shud say, ‘We'r naethin oot o tha ordinarie! Fer we hae daen nae mair ner we haed tae.’ ” An sae Jesus went on tae Jerusalem, follaein tha mairch atween Samaria an Galilee.  As he went ïntae yin o tha vïllages, he saa ten men that wur lepers stannin a wyes aff, an the' caad oot tae hïm, “Jesus, Maistèr, tak peetie on iz!”  An whaniver he saa thaim, he saed, “Awa tae tha preeshts an let thaim luk at ye.” An lo an behoul, as the' went thair wye, the' wur hailt!  An yin o thaim, whan he saen he wus cured, turnt bak an cryed oot at tha tap o hïs voice, “Praise God!” Then he faad doon at Jesus' feet an gien thenks. An tha man wus a Samaritan, sae he wus.  “Dïd A no cure ten men?” axt Jesus. “Whar's tha ither nine? Hae nane o thaim cum bak tae gie thenks tae God apairt frae thïs foreigner?”  Jesus saed tae tha man, “Rise up an gang yer wye, yer faith haes made ye weel.” Yin time whaniver tha Pharisees axt Jesus whan God's Kïngdom wud cum, he toul thaim, “Yis cannae say, ‘Here ït ïs!’ or ‘Thair ït ïs!’ Tha Kïngdom o God ïs aareadie here amang yis , sae thair's nae use lukkin fer ït cumin!” An he saed tae hïs follaers, “Tha day wull cum whan yis'll want tae see tha Sinn o Man. Yis'll luk fer me an A'll no be here.  Fowk micht say, ‘He's here or he's thair’, but tak nae notysh, an dïnnae rin eftèr thaim.  Fer jist as tha lichtnin fleshes ower tha lïft, that's whut laik ït'll be, tha day tha Sinn o Man cums bak.  But afore that, He'll hae tae suffer sair, an tha fowk roon hïm noo wull turn agin hïm.  Whaniver tha Sinn o Man cums bak, ït'll be jist laik ït wus ïn Noah's day.  Fer fowk wus aitin an drïnkin an gettin merriet, richt up tae tha verie day Noah went ïntae tha airk, then tha wattèr floodit an aa wur droont.  It wull be tha same as ït wus ïn tha time o Lot; the' et an the' drunk an the' cairriet on wi thair bïzness o buyin, sellin, fairmin an biggin.  But tha verie day that Lot went oot o Sodom, fire an brimstane cum doon frae heiven an the' wur aa kïllt.  Tha same wull happen tha day yis see tha Sinn o Man cum bak.  On that day, naebodie shud lea hïs ruiftap  an be gaun bak doon fer ocht ïn hïs hoose, an naebodie shud lea hïs fiel ether, tae gae bak hame.  Mine whut happent tae Lot's guidwife!  Whaiver houls on tae hïs life wull loass ït, an whaiver gies up hïs life wull aye hae ït.  A'm tellin yis, ïn that nicht, twa fowk wull be ïn tha yin bed; yin wull be tuk an tha ither lef behin.  Twa weemen wull be grindin mail thegither; yin wull be tuk an tha ither lef behin. [ Twa men wull be ïn tha fiel; tha yin wull be tuk an tha ither lef behin.]”  An hïs follaers axt hïm, “Whar wull thïs tak place?” An Jesus toul thaim, “Whar ye see a crood o vultèrs, ye know thair's a deid bodie aboot. Ay, sae whaniver ye see tha signs A'm taakin aboot, then ye'll know weel eneuch!” Jesus toul hïs follaers thïs parable, that meent that the' shud aye pray an no gie up.  An ït went laik thïs: “Thair wus thïs judge ïn a bïg toon, that haed nae fear o ether God ner man, an haed nae thocht fer oniebodie.  In that same toon thair wus thïs weeda wumman, that kep on cumin tae tha judge, sayin, ‘Wud ye mak shair A get a fair dail ïn tha coort frae tha yin that's agin me?’  At tha stairt tha judge niver bothert: fer a lang time he dïd naethin. But then he saed tae hissel, ‘Tha mair A dïnnae fear God or care aboot fowk, still wi aa, A wull halp oot thïs weeda wumman, fer she's giein me that much bother. A'm scunnèrt wi hir aye rinnin tae me!’ ”  Tha Loard went on, “Yis unnèrstan whut tha baad judge ïs sayin.  Dae yis no thïnk God wull tak tha pairt o hïs ain fowk that cry oot tae hïm day an nicht? He'll no keep pittin thaim aff, sae he'll no.  A'm tellin yis, He'll no be lang ïn seein justice daen. But whaniver tha Sinn o Man cums bak, A wunnèr wull he fin oniebodie wi faith on tha irth?” An he toul anither parable tae tha yins that wus fu o thairsels, an thocht the' wur aa richt, an lukt doon on ithers.  “Thair wus twa men went up tae tha Hoose o God fer tae pray. Yin wus a Pharisee an tha ither wus a tex man.  Tha Pharisee ris tae hïs feet, an prayed tae hissel: ‘O God, A thenk ye that A'm no laik ither fowk, ner fer that mettèr laik thon tex boy ower thonner! A dïnnae chait fowk, A dae naethin wrang, an A keep tae me ain wife. A fast twice ïn tha week, an A gie a tenth o aa A hae.’  But tha tex man stud awa bak, an wudnae as much as lïft hïs een tae heiven, but he bate hïs breesht ïn sorra, an saed, ‘O God, hae mercie on me, fer A'm naethin but a sïnner!’  A tell ye, thïs tex man, an no tha Pharisee, went doon tae hïs hoose ïn guid stannin wi God. Fer tha yin that thïnks a lock o hissel wull be brocht doon, but tha yin that's hummle wull be lïftit up.” An as weel, the' brocht wee weans tae Jesus, sae that he cud pit hïs hans on thaim tae bliss thaim. But whaniver tha follaers saen thïs, the' chackt tha fowk.  But Jesus toul thaim tae cum on aheid, an saed, “Alloo tha weans tae cum tae me; dïnnae stap thaim, fer tha Kïngdom o God belangs tae tha laik o these.  A'm tellin ye, whaiver daesnae tak tha Kïngdom o God ïntae hïs hairt laik a wean daes, wull no get ïn ava.” Yinst an impoartin bodie axt hïm, “Guid Maistèr, whut maun A dae tae be shair A get tae heiven an leeve fer iver?”  An Jesus saed bak tae hïm, “Why ir ye caain me guid? Thair's naebodie guid, apairt frae God.  Ye weel ken tha commauns: ‘Dïnnae commït adultèrie’; ‘dïnnae murdèr’; ‘dïnnae tak whut's no yer ain’; ‘dïnnae tell lees aboot ither fowk’; an ‘gie respeck tae yer faither an yer mither.’ ”  An tha bodie saed bak tae hïm, “A hae daen aa these thïngs since A wus onie age.”  Whan Jesus heerd thïs, he saed tae tha man, “Thair's jist yin thïng ye still hae tae dae. Sell aa ye hae an gie tae thaim that haesnae much, an ye'll hae walth ïn heiven. An then cum bak an follae me!”  Noo whaniver tha man heerd thïs he wus doon ïn tha mooth, fer he haed a wile lock o money.  An whaniver Jesus saa tha wye tha man tuk ït, he saed, “Hoo verie haird ït ïs fer thaim that haes money tae git ïntae tha Kïngdom o God!  Fer ït wud be aisier fer a kemel tae gae throu tha ee o a needle, ner fer a monied man tae git ïntae tha Kïngdom o God.”  An tha yins that heerd ït axt, “Wha ïn aa tha warl can be saved then?”  An Jesus saed, “Thaim thïngs men cannae dae, God's mair ner fït tae dae!”  Wi that, Petèr saed, “Mine, we hae left iveriethin behin an follaed ye!”  An Jesus saed tae thaim, “A'm tellin yis, oniebodie that haes left hïs hoose, hïs faither an mither, brithers, wife or weans fer tha sake o tha Kïngdom o God wull dae weel an hae plentie ïn thïs warl; an ïn tha warl tae cum he wull hae iverlastin life.” Then he tuk tha Twal tae tha side an he saed tae thaim, “See here, we'r gaun up tae Jerusalem, an aa that's bin writ doon bi tha proaphits aboot tha Sinn o Man wull tak place thair.  Fer he'll be hannit ower tae tha Gentiles fer thaim tae mak fun o hïm, trait hïm ïll an spït on hïm.  An the' wull gie hïm a whuppin an kïll hïm, but on tha thurd day he wull rise tae life agane.”  But the' dïdnae unnèrstan onie o tha thïngs he saed, fer tha mainin wus hïd frae thaim, an the' jist cudnae tak ït ïn. Noo whan Jesus wus cumin up tae Jericho, on tha ootskirts, a blin man wus sïttin beggin on tha bunker o tha róad.  Whan he heerd tha thrang gaun bye, he axt whut ït wus aa aboot,  an the' toul hïm, “Jesus o Nazareth ïs cumin.”  Tha blin man cryed oot, “Jesus, Sinn o Davit, tak peetie on me!”  An tha yins that went afore Jesus scoult tha beggar an the' toul hïm tae be quait, but he guldèrt aa tha mair, “Sinn o Davit, tak peetie on me!”  An Jesus stapt an saed, “Brïng tha blin man tae me!” An whan the' dïd, Jesus axt hïm,  “Whut dae ye want me tae dae fer ye?” An he saed, “Loard, A want tae be able tae see agane.”  An Jesus saed bak tae hïm, “Hae yer sicht! Yer faith haes made ye hale.”  Richt awa he cud see agane, an he follaed Jesus, giein glorie tae God. An whaniver aa tha ither fowk saa thïs, the' gien praise tae God as weel. An Jesus cum tae tha toon o Jericho, an wus trevelin throu ït.  Noo, thair wus thïs man caad Zacchaeus, that wus a heid tex man, an he wus quare an weel-aff.  An he wus wantin tae see fer hissel whut Jesus wus laik, but he wus a wee man, an he cudnae get near Jesus fer tha crood.  Sae he run awa on aheid, an shïnned up a sycomore fïg tree alang tha wye, tae hae a guid luk at Jesus whan he wus gaun bye.  An whan Jesus cum tae tha tree, he lukt up an saed til hïm, “Zacchaeus, git doon or that richt noo! Fer A'm gaun tae yer hoose tha day!”  Sae Zacchaeus lep doon oot o tha tree, an tuk hïm hame an gien hïm a wile guid walcum.  Aa tha fowk saen thïs, an stairtit tae pass remairks, sayin, “He's stappin ower wi a wrangdaer!”  Oniehoo, Zacchaeus stud up an toul Jesus, “A tell ye whut, Loard. A'll gie tha half o whut A hae tae thaim at haes need o ït. An ïf A hae got oniethin bi chaitin, A'll pye ït bak fower times ower.”  An Jesus saed, “Salvation haes cum tae thïs hoose tha day, fer thïs man ïs a sinn o Abraham as weel!  A masel, tha Sinn o Man, hae cum tae luk fer thaim at's loast, an tae save thaim.” An tha hale crood tuk tent o whut Jesus wus sayin. An as Jerusalem wus nearhan, he stairtit tae tell thaim a parable, fer fowk thocht that tha Kïngdom o God wus gaun tae cum aboot at yinst.  He toul thaim thïs: “A weel boarn man went awa tae a faur-aff lan. He wus tae hae hissel crooned kïng, an then he wus tae cum bak agane.  Afore he went but, he caad ten o hïs sarvin men, an gien each o thaim yin gowld coin , an he saed tae thaim, ‘Tak thïs catter an mak tha maist o ït, tae A cum bak.’  But he wusnae weel thocht o amang hïs ain fowk, an sae the' sent oot wurd eftèr he went awa, sayin, ‘We dïnnae want thïs man tae rule ower iz.’  But he got tae be kïng aa tha same, an he cum bak hame. Then he oardèrt tha sarvin men tae gie an accoont o hoo the' haed daen wi tha catter he haed gien thaim.  Tha furst yin toul hïm, ‘Loard, yer coin haes made ten mair.’  ‘Weel daen!’ saed tha kïng. ‘Ye ir a guid sarvint. Ye hae showed A can trust ye ïn wee thïngs. A'll gie ye ten cïties tae rin!’  An tha saicont yin cum an saed, ‘Loard, yer coin haes made five coins.’  An tha kïng saed, ‘A'll gie ye five cïties tae rin.’  Wi that, anither yin cum up an saed, ‘Luk, Loard, here's yer coin. A hae kep ït lapt up ïn a cloot.  A wus feart o ye, fer ye ir a haird man tae dail wi. Ye tak whut daesnae belang tae ye, an ye hairvest whut ye hinnae plantit.’  Tha kïng cum bak wi, ‘Ye uisless guid-fer-naethin! Frae yer ain mooth ye hae condemned yersel. Sae ye thocht A wus a haird man, dïd ye, takkin whut dïdnae belang tae me, an hairvestin whut A haednae plantit?  Weel, ye cud hae püt ma siller ïntae tha bank; hoo cum ye dïdnae? Then whaniver A cum bak, ït cud hae made me a wee bït o ïntrèst!’  Wi that, tha kïng toul thaim that wur stannin roon aboot, ‘Tak hïs coin frae hïm, an gie ït tae hïm that haes tha ten.’  But the' saed tae hïm, ‘Loard, shair he haes ten coin!’  Saed tha kïng, ‘A'll tell ye thïs, iverie yin that haes wull be gien mair; an whaiver haes lïttle or naethin, even whut he haes wull be taen awa frae hïm!  But as fer thaim that wur agin me an wudnae hae me fer kïng, brïng thaim here tae me, an kïll thaim fornent me!’ ” Eftèr tellin thaim aa thïs, Jesus went on aheid alang tha róad up tae Jerusalem.
