That's tha raison hïs mither an faither saed, “He's oul eneuch, ax hïm yersels.” Then tha man at wus blin wus brocht up afore thaim a saicont time. “God's yer wutness, sae taak tha truith noo,” the' saed. “We ken thïs man Jesus ïs a sïnner.”  “A cudnae say,” qo he, “whuther he's a sïnner or no. Yin thïng A dae ken but. Yinst A wus blin, an noo A can see!”  But the' kep on at hïm, “Whut dïd he dae tae ye? Hoo dïd he apen yer een?”  He reponed, “A toul ye afore an ye wudnae lïsten! Whut dae ye want tae hear ït agane fer? Dae yous want tae stairt follaein hïm anaa?”  The' yaukt hïm an saed, “You ir a follaer o thon fella, but we ir follaers o Moses here.  We ken that God spauk wi Moses, but we dïnnae even ken whar thïs fella cums frae.”  Tha man answert, “Weel, that bates aa! Ye dïnnae ken whar he cums frae, yit he apent ma een.  We ken that God daesnae lïsten tae sïnners. But he wull lïsten tae yin that's God-fearin an daes hïs wull.  Frae tha warl begun, ye niver heerd tell o summodie apenin tha een o a man boarn blin, dïd ye?  If thïs man wusnae frae God, he cudnae a daen ocht ava.”  The' cum bak at hïm, “You wur boarn steepit ïn sïn, an noo ye wud dar tae taich iz!” An the' throwed hïm oot. Jesus heerd wurd the' haed throwed hïm oot, an whaniver he fun hïm, he axt hïm, “Dae ye believe ïn tha Sinn o Man?”  “Wha ïs he, sïr?” tha man axt. “Tell iz sae A can believe ïn hïm.”  “Ye hae saen hïm,” saed Jesus, “In fect, ye'r lukkin at hïm! It's hïm that's taakin tae ye!”  Then tha man saed, “Loard, A believe!” An he wurshipt hïm.  Jesus saed, “It's fer judgemen A'm cum ïntae thïs warl: thaim that ir blin A'll mak tae see; an thaim that can see, A'll show thaim that the' ir blin.”  But some Pharisees that wur nearhan heerd hïm say thïs, an the' axt, “Whut? Ir ye sayin we'r blin anaa?”  Jesus telt thaim, “Weel, ïf yis wur blin, ye wudnae be guiltie o sïn; but noo yis mak oot ye can see, yer guilt bides on ye.” “Noo here's tha truith o ït,” qo Jesus, “tha man that daesnae cum ïntae tha ree bi tha yett, tae get amang tha sheep, but spiels ïn bi some ither róad, ye can be shair he's a thief or a reiver.  Tha man that cums ïn bi tha yett ïs tha hird o tha sheep.  Tha herd-han apens tha yett fer hïm, an tha sheep hear tha shepherd's voice. He caas hïs sheep bi name an leads thaim oot eftèr hïm.  Whaniver he haes brocht oot aa hïs ain sheep, he waaks aheid o thaim, an hïs sheep follae hïm, fer the' ken hïs voice.  The'll no follae a stranger but; na, the'll rin aff whan the' hear a voice the' dïnnae ken.”  Jesus gien thaim thïs pictèr tae pit ower hïs mainin, but the' dïdnae unnèrstan whut he wus taakin aboot. Sae Jesus toul thaim yinst mair, “Here's tha truith o ït. A be tha yett fer tha sheep.  Aa thaim that cum afore me wus thiefs an reivers, but tha sheep tuk nae heed o thaim.  A be tha yett; hïm that cums ïn throu me wull be saved. He wull gang ïn an oot, an fin guid gress.  Tha thief jist cums fer tae wreck an rob an kïll; A hae cum that the' micht hae life, an hae ït ower an abain. A be tha guid shepherd. Tha guid shepherd gies hïs ain life fer tha sheep.  Tha hired han ïs no tha shepherd, an he daesnae own tha sheep ether. Sae whan he sees a wolf cumin, he rins aff an leas thaim. An then tha wolf lays hoult o tha flock an skails ït.  Tha man rins awa, fer he ïs a hired han an he cares naethin fer tha sheep.  A be tha guid shepherd; A ken ma sheep an ma sheep ken me - jist laik tha Faither kens me an A ken tha Faither - an A gie ma ain life fer tha sheep.  A hae ither sheep that daesnae belang tae thïs ree. A maun brïng thaim forbye. The'll tak heed o ma voice anaa, an thair wull be yin hirsle an yin shepherd.  Tha raison ma Faither loves me ïs thïs: A gie up ma ain life - jist fer tae tak ït bak agane.  Naebodie taks ït frae me, but A gie ït up o ma ain wull. A hae tha thortie tae gie ït up, an A hae tha thortie tae tak ït bak agane. Thïs ïs tha chairge A hae got frae ma Faither.” Becas o whut he saed, tha Jews wur at odds wi yin anither yit agane.  Monie o thaim saed, “He's bin tuk ower wi a divil, an he's haiverin! Whut wud ye lïsten tae hïm fer?”  But ithers saed, “Thon's no tha wurds o a man taen ower wi a divil. Cud a divil apen tha een o tha blin?” Roon cum tha Faist o Dedication . It wus wuntèrtim, an Jesus wus ïn tha Temple gruns, waakin alang unnèr Solomon's Airches.  Tha Jews gethert roon Jesus, quïzzin hïm, “Hoo lang wull ye keep iz wunnèrin? We'r deein tae fin oot. If ye'r tha Christ, tell iz strecht!”  Jesus reponed, “A hae aareadie toul ye, but yis dïnnae believe me. Tha warks A dae ïn ma Faither's name baks me up, but tha raison yis dïnnae believe me ïs that ye'r no ma sheep.  Ma sheep hears ma caa; A ken thaim, an the' follae me.  A gie thaim ayelastin life, an the' wull niver perish; naebodie can wheek thaim oot o ma han.  Ma Faither, that gien thaim tae me, ïs ower ocht; naebodie can wheek thaim oot o ma Faither's han.  Me an tha Faither ïs yin.” Yinst mair tha Jews gethert stanes fer tae clod hïm.  But Jesus toul thaim, “A hae showed ye onie amoont o guid warks wrocht bi tha Faither. Whut yin o thaim ir ye stanein me fer?”  “We'r no stanein ye fer ocht o thaim,” tha Jews reponed, “but fer blesphemie! You ir jist an ordinarie man, an yit ye mak yersel oot tae be God.”  Jesus answert thaim, “Is ït no writ ïn yer ain Laa: ‘A hae toul ye, yis ir gods’?  Noo, ïf he caad thaimins that tha wurd o God cum tae, ‘gods’ - an mine you, tha Scrïptures stan fer iver an aye - whut aboot tha yin that tha Faither set apairt as hïs verie ain an sent ïntae tha warl? A saed, ‘A be God's Sinn’, an fer that yis chairge me wi blesphemie?  If A'm no daein tha thïngs ma Faither daes, then dïnnae believe me.  But ïf A dae thaim, tha mair ye dïnnae believe whut A tell ye, jist believe whut tha warks thairsels tells ye. That wye yis'll unnèrstan fer shair that tha Faither ïs ïn me, an me ïn tha Faither.”  Agane the' tried tae lay houl o hïm, but he gien thaim tha slip! Eftèr that, Jesus gaed bak ower tha Joardan tae tha place whar Jhone baptised at tha furst. He stapt thonner a wee while,  an monie fowk cum tae hïm. The' saed, “Fer aa that Jhone niver daen onie mïraclis signs, iveriethin Jhone saed aboot thïs man wus tha truith.”  An ïn thon place monie fowk püt thair faith ïn Jesus. Thair wus thïs man the' caad Lazarus an he wusnae verie weel. He wus frae Bethanie, a wee toon whar hïs sïstèrs Mary an Mairtha leeved.  Noo thïs wus tha same Mary that poored scent on tha Loard an gien hïs feet a dicht wi hir hair. It wus hir brither that wus no weel.  Sae tha twa sïstèrs sent wurd tae Jesus, sayin, “Loard, tha yin ye love ïs seeck.”  Whaniver Jesus heerd tell o ït, he saed, “Thïs ailment wull no enn up wi hïm deein. Na, ït's fer tha glorie o God, an fer tha Sinn o God tae get tha glorie oot o ït.” Mairtha an hir sïstèr an Lazarus wus aa loved bi Jesus,  sae tha mair he heerd Lazarus wusnae weel, he stapt fer twa mair days whar he wus at.  Then eftèr thïs he toul hïs follaers, “Cum on an we'll gang bak tae Judea.”  “But Rabbi,” the' saed, “a wee while bak thaim Jews wus gaun tae stane ye, an noo ye'r fer gaun bak thonner?”  Jesus saed, “Is thair no twal oors o daylicht iverie day? If ye waak ïn tha braid daylicht ye'll no thrip an faa, fer ye can see bi tha licht o thïs warl.  It's whan ye'r waakin bi nicht that ye thrip up, fer ye hinnae tha licht ïn ye.”  Eftèr he saed thïs, he went on, “Oor freen Lazarus ïs jist sleepin; but A'm awa fer tae waaken hïm up.”  Hïs follaers reponed, “Weel Loard, ïf he's jist haein a sleep, he'll shuin be on tha men.”  Hïs follaers thocht he wus taakin aboot ordinarie sleep, but Jesus wus mainin Lazarus wus deid.  Sae then he toul thaim strecht, “Lazarus ïs deid.  An fer your sake, A'm gled A wusnae thair, sae that you micht believe; cum on noo, an we'll gang til hïm.”  Then Tammas (caad Didymus ) saed tae tha ither follaers, “Cum on an we'll gang tae, sae that we can dee alang wi hïm!” Whaniver Jesus got nixt Bethanie, he fun that Lazarus haed bin fower days deid an ïn tha tomb.  Bethanie wus nearhan Jerusalem, aboot twa mile doon tha róad.  An a hale lock o Jews haed cum tae Mairtha an Mary fer tae stan bye thaim ïn tha loass o thair brither.  Whan Mairtha got wurd that Jesus wus cumin, oot she went tae meet hïm, but Mary sut ïn tha hoose.  “Loard,” Mairtha saed tae Jesus, “If you haed hae bin here, ma brither wudnae be deid.  But A ken that even noo God wull gie ye whutiver ye ax hïm.”  Jesus saed til hir, “Yer brither wull rise agane.”  Mairtha answert, “A ken he wull rise agane ïn tha resurrection, on tha hinmaist day.”  Jesus telt hir, “A be tha resurrection an tha life. Hïm that believes ïn me, tha mair he dees, yit he'll leeve agane;  an whaiver leeves an believes ïn me wull niver dee. Dae ye believe thïs?”  “Ay, Loard, A dae!” qo she. “A believe that you ir tha Christ, tha Sinn o God, tha yin we wur toul wus cumin ïntae tha warl.” An eftèr she saed that, awa she went bak hame an tuk hir sïstèr Mary tae tha yin side. “Tha Maistèr ïs here,” qo she, “an he wants ye tae cum.”  Whaniver Mary heerd that, up she got ïn a hurrie an gaed til hïm.  Noo Jesus haednae yit got tha lenth o tha vïllage, but wus still bak at tha spot whar Mairtha haed met up wi hïm.  Tha Jews that wus thair ïn tha hoose tae offer Mary sorra fer hir trouble, whaniver the' saa tha quïck she got up an went oot, up they got as weel an went oot eftèr hir, jalousin she wus awa tae tha tomb tae greet thonner.  Sae Mary got tae whar Jesus wus at, an whaniver she saa hïm, she faad doon at hïs feet an she saed, “Loard, ïf you haed hae bin here, ma brither wudnae be deid!”  Whan Jesus saa hir greetin, an aa tha Jews that wur cum alang wi hir greetin forbye, he wus vext ïn hïs spïrit, an he wus hairt sair.  “Whar hae yis püt hïm?” saed he. “Cum an see, Loard,” the' toul hïm.  Wi that, Jesus begun tae greet.  Tha Jews saed, “See tha much he loved hïm!”  But some o thaim saed, “If he cud apen tha een o thon blin man, cud he no hae kep thïs man frae deein?” Jesus cum tae tha tomb an hïs hairt wus troublet agane. It wus a cave wi a stane püt ower ïts mooth.  “Tak tha stane awa,” qo he. “But Loard,” saed Mairtha, tha deid man's sïstèr, “bi noo ït wud stink ye oot, fer he's ïn thair thïs fower days.”  Wi that Jesus saed, “Dïd A no tell ye that ïf ye believed, ye wud see tha glorie o God?”  Sae the' shïftit tha stane, an Jesus lukt up tae heiven abain an he saed, “Faither, A gie ye thenks that ye hae heerd me.  Ye hear me ayewyes, A know that; but A hae saed aa thïs fer tha guid o tha fowk stud here. Sae the' micht believe that you sent me.”  Whaniver he saed that, Jesus caad oot at tha tap o hïs voice, “Lazarus, cum on oot!”  An lo an behoul, tha deid man dïd cum oot, hïs hans an feet lapt wi strïps o linen, an a cloot roon hïs face. Jesus toul thaim, “Tak tha grave claes aff hïm, an let hïm gang.” Wi that, monie o tha Jews that wur cum tae be at tha wake wi Mary, whaniver the' saa whut Jesus dïd, the' püt thair faith ïn hïm.  But ithers amang thaim went an toul tha Pharisees whut Jesus haed daen.  An sae tha heid preeshts an tha Pharisees caad tha Cooncil thegither. “Is thïs no a hanlin? Whut'll we dae?” the' axt. “Fer thon man's daein a hale wheen o mïraclis signs.  If we let hïm aff wi ït, tha nixt thïng the'll aa believe on hïm, an then tha Romans'll cum an dae awa wi baith oor halie place an oor kintrie on iz.”  An then yin o thaim bi tha name o Caiaphas, that wus Heich Preesht thon yeir, spauk oot, “Yis ken naethin ava!  Ye dïnnae unnèrstan that ït wud be fer tha best ïf yin man deed fer aa tha fowk, ay, faur bettèr ner fer tha hale kintrie tae be wiped oot!”  He dïdnae say thïs o hïs ain accoard, but as Heich Preesht thon yeir he foretelt that Jesus wud dee fer tha hale nation.  An no jist fer thon nation, but fer aa tha skailt childèr o God, tae brïng thaim thegither an mak thaim yin.  Sae frae that day an oor the' collogued thegither tae dae hïm ïn. An eftèr that Jesus wudnae cum oot ïn tha apen onie mair amang tha Jews. Rether he tuk hissel aff tae a pairt o tha kintrie nearhan tha wuldèrness, tae a toon bi tha name o Ephraim; an he stapt ower thair wi hïs follaers. Whaniver ït wus near time fer tha Passower Faist, monie fowk frae tha kintrie went up tae Jerusalem fer tae get thair rïtual waash afore tha Passower.  The' kep lukkin fer Jesus, an as the' stud roon ïn tha Temple gruns, the' axt yin anither, “Dae ye thïnk, ïs he fer cumin tae tha Faist ava?”  But tha heid preeshts an Pharisees haed gien oardèrs that ïf oniebodie fun oot tha wharaboots o Jesus, the' maun let thaim know, sae as the' cud hae hïm lïftit. Sïx day afore tha Passower, Jesus cum tae Bethanie whar Lazarus leeved, hïm Jesus haed ris frae tha deid.  The' wur houlin a dennèr thonner fer Jesus. Mairtha wus sarvin at ït, an Lazarus wus yin o thaim roon tha boord wi Jesus.  Weel, Mary tuk aboot a pint o pure nard, a scentit oyle that coast bïg money, an she poored ït ower Jesus's feet an gien thaim a dicht wi hir hair. An tha hoose wus fu o tha sweet scent o tha oyle.  But yin o hïs follaers, Judas Iscariot, hïm that wud bethray hïm latèr on, he wus agin ït.  “Hoo cum thïs oyle wusnae soul an tha catter gien tae tha puir? It'd tak ye a year tae wark fer that!”  He dïdnae say that oot o peetie fer tha puir, but becas he wus a thief. He kep tha siller-pooch an he jist dïppt ïntae ït fer hïs ain use whan he wantit.  “Lea hir be,” Jesus reponed, “she wus supposed tae keep thïs scent bak fer ma layin oot tae be buriet.  Fer tha puir ye'll aye hae wi yis, but ye'll no aye hae me.” Bi noo a bïg thrang o Jews haed gethert whaniver the' fun oot that Jesus wus thair. The' wurnae cum jist on accoont o Jesus, but wur lukkin a wee skellie o Lazarus forbye, hïm that Jesus haed ris frae tha deid.  Sae tha heid preeshts collogued thegither tae kïll Lazarus as weel,  Fer ït wus ower tha heid o hïm that monie o tha Jews wur noo pittin thair faith ïn Jesus. Tha nixt day, a bïg thrang o fowk that haed cum fer tha Passower heerd wurd that Jesus wus makkin hïs róad fer Jerusalem.  An the' tuk brenches o palm-trees an oot the' went tae meet hïm, cryin, “Hosanna! Blisst be tha Yin that cums ïn tha name o tha Loard! Blisst be tha Kïng o Israel!” Jesus fun a young cuddie, an sut on ïts bak, jist laik ït's writ doon, “Dïnnae be feart, O Dochtèr o Zion, Luk see, yer kïng ïs cumin, Sut on a young cuddie.” At tha stairt, hïs follaers dïdnae unnèrstan aa thïs. It wusnae tae eftèr Jesus cum ïntae hïs glorie that the' twigged that thaim thïngs wus writ aboot hïm an haed happent tae hïm.  Noo tha crood that wus wi hïm whaniver he caad Lazarus frae tha tomb an ris hïm frae tha deid wus taakin aboot ït aa ower tha kintrie;  an that wus why sitch a crood o fowk went oot fer tae meet hïm, acause the'd heerd aboot tha mïraclis sign he'd daen.  Sae tha Pharisees collogued amang thairsels, “Luk, we'r gettin naewhar wi thïs. Tha hale warl's rinnin eftèr hïm!” Noo thair wus some Greeks amang tha fowk that haed cum up fer tha Passower.  The' made an approach tae Phïlip, wha cum frae Bethsaida ïn Galilee. “Sïr,” the' saed, “we'r lukkin tae hae a wurd wi Jesus.”  Aff Phïlip went an toul Andra; an then Andra an Phïlip thegither telt Jesus. Tha answer Jesus gien wus thïs: “Noo's tha time fer tha Sinn o Man tae cum ïntae hïs glorie.  Here's tha truith o ït. Less an ear o seed-coarn draps doon ïntae tha grun an dees, ït jist stays on ïts lane. But ïf ït dees, ït maks a hale lock o seeds.  Hïm that's ower fand o hïs ain life wull loass ït, but hïm at haes nae gra fer leevin ïn thïs warl, wull keep hïs life fer iver an aye.  Oniebodie that wants me as thair maistèr maun follae me; an whar A'm at, ye'll fin ma sarvint thonner forbye. Ma Faither wull gie honour tae hïm that sarves me. An noo ma hairt ïs sair annoyt; whut am A tae say? ‘Faither, save me frae thïs oor’? Na, fer ït wus fer thïs verie raison that A'm cum tae thïs oor.  Faither, glorie be tae yer name!” An wi that a voice cum frae heiven, an ït saed, “A hae gien ït tha glorie, an A'll gie ït tha glorie agane.”  Whaniver tha crood thonner heerd ït, the' thocht ït wus a rummle o thunnèr; but ithers saed ït wus an angel taakin wi hïm.  Jesus saed, “Thon voice wus fer your guid, no fer mine.  Noo ïs tha time o judgemen fer thïs warl; noo tha prince o thïs warl wull be driv oot.  But whaniver A'm lïftit up frae tha irth, A wull draa iveriebodie tae masel.”  He saed thïs tae pit ït oot ïn tha apen whut wye he wus gaun tae dee.  Tha crood saed, “Oor Laa tells iz that tha Christ wull bide fer iver, sae hoo cum ye can say, ‘Tha Sinn o Man maun be lïftit up?’ Thïs ‘Sinn o Man’, wha wud he be oniehoo?”  Wi that, Jesus toul thaim, “Yis wull hae tha licht jist a wee while lang'r. Waak ïn tha licht whaniver ye hae ït, afore tha mirk cums doon on ye. Thaim that waak ïn tha mirk dïnnae ken whar the'r fer.  Pit yer trust ïn tha licht as lang as ye hae ït, sae as ye can becum childèr o tha licht.” Whan Jesus wus daen taakin, he went awa an hud hissel frae thaim. Tha mair Jesus wrocht aa thae mïraclis signs afore thaim, the' still wudnae believe ïn hïm.  That wus tae brïng aboot whut Isaiah tha proaphit haed saed: “Loard, whar ir tha yins that hae tuk oor wurd tae hairt, An wha ir tha yins that hae wutnesst your pooer?” But the' wurnae able tae believe, fer laik Isaiah says ïn anither pairt: “He haes made thair een blin an turnt thair hairts tae stane, Sae the' can see naethin wi thair een, ner unnèrstan ocht wi thair hairts, Ner turn, fer me tae hail thaim.” Isaiah wus taakin aboot Jesus whaniver he saed thïs; he lukt aheid an foresaa hïs glorie.  Wi aa that, thair wus monies a yin dïd believe ïn hïm, even amang tha heidyins. But the' wudnae own up tae thair faith afore tha Pharisees, fer fear o bein püt oot o tha Meetin Hoose.  Fer the' wur mair keen on bein weel thocht o bi men ner bi God. Then Jesus caad oot, “Whan a bodie haes belief ïn me, he daesnae jist believe ïn me masel, but ïn tha Yin that sent me.  Hïm that sees me, sees tha Yin that sent me.  A'm cum ïntae tha warl as a licht, sae that naebodie that believes ïn me shud bide ïn tha dairk.  Anent oniebodie that haes heerd ma wurds, but daesnae houl tae thaim, A'm no fer makkin judgemen on hïm. Fer A dïdnae cum ïntae tha warl tae judge ït, but tae save ït.  Thair ïs a judge fer tha yin that turns hïs bak on me an daesnae tak ma wurds tae hairt; tha verie wurds A spauk wull judge hïm on tha day o Reckonin.  Fer A wusnae taakin on ma ain accoont, but tha Faither that sent me toul me whut tae say, an hoo tae say ït.  An A know richt weel that hïs commauns aye róads tae iverlastin life. Sae ocht A say ïs jist whut tha Faither haes bïd me say.” Noo tha Passower Faist wus nearhan, an Jesus knowed that tha time wus cum fer hïm tae lea thïs warl an gang til tha Faither. Haein loved hïs ain that wus ïn tha warl, noo he apent up tae thaim tha fu meesure o hïs love.  Supper wus gettin püt oot, an tha deil haed aareadie püt tha thocht ïntae tha hairt o Judas Iscariot, sinn o Simon, tae bethray Jesus.  Jesus knowed that tha Faither haed gien aa thïngs ïntae hïs pooer, an that he wus cum frae God an wus fer gaun bak tae God;  Sae up he got frae tha supper, tuk aff hïs ooter claes, an roon hïs mïddle he lapt a dryin cloot.  Eftèr that, he teemed wattèr ïntae a boul an stairtit tae waash tha feet o hïs follaers, an gien thaim a dicht wi tha dryin cloot lapt roon aboot hïm.  He cum tae Simon Petèr, wha axt hïm, “Loard, you ir no fer waashin ma feet, ir ye?”  Jesus answert, “Ye dïnnae get whut A'm daein jist noo, but latèr on ye'll unnèrstan.”  “Na,” qo Petèr, “ye'll niver waash ma feet!” Jesus toul hïm, “Less A gie ye a waash, ye'll hae nae pairt wi me.”  “Weel, Loard,” Simon Petèr reponed, “no jist ma feet then, but ma hans an ma heid anaa!”  Jesus answert, “A bodie that haes waasht hissel aa ower, jist needs tae dae hïs feet; fer he's aareadie clain. An you follaers ir clain, sae ye ir, but thair's yin amang ye that ïsnae.”  Fer he knowed wha wud bethray hïm, an that wus fer why he saed that no iverie last yin o thaim wus clain. Whaniver he wus daen waashin thair feet, he püt hïs robe bak on an he tuk hïs place agane. “Dae yis no ken whut A hae daen fer ye?” he axt thaim.  “Yis caa me ‘Taicher’ an ‘Loard’, an ye'r richt, fer that's wha A am.  An noo that A masel, yer Loard an Taicher, hae waasht yer feet, you shud waash yin anither's feet tae.  A daen ït masel tae show yis tae dae whut A hae daen fer you.  Here's tha truith o ït. Nae sarvint ïs bïgger ner hïs maistèr, an hïm at brïngs a message ïsnae bïgger ner tha yin that sent hïm.  Noo that yis ken these thïngs, ye'll be blisst ïf ye dae thaim. A'm no taakin aboot yis aa; A ken thaimins A hae waaled. But thïs ïs tae brïng aboot whut's writ doon ïn tha halie Scrïptures: ‘Hïm that shares ma breid wi me haes turnt agin me.’  A'm tellin ye noo aforehan, sae that whaniver ït cums aboot, yis'll believe that A be tha Messiah.  Thair's no twa wyes aboot ït. Whaiver walcums oniebodie A senn walcums me, an whaiver walcums me, walcums tha Yin that sent me.” Eftèr he saed that, Jesus's spïrit wus gye vext; then he stapt an cum oot wi thïs: “A'm tellin ye strecht, yin o yis ïs fer bethrayin me!”  Hïs follaers jist gaukt at yin anither. Whutch yin o thaim wus he taakin aboot?  Yin amang thaim, tha follaer that Jesus loved, wus leant bak agin hïm.  Simon Petèr catched thon follaer's ee, an he saed, “Wha's he taakin aboot?”  Sae leanin bak agin Jesus, that follaer speered, “Loard, wha ïs ït?”  Jesus answert, “It'll be tha yin A gie thïs bït o breid tae, eftèr A hae dunkt ït ïn tha boul.” An he dunkt tha bït o breid an gien ït tae Judas Iscariot, tha sinn o Simon.  Tha mïnit Judas tuk tha breid, tha Deil wus ïn hïm. “Whut ye'r fer daein,” Jesus telt hïm, “dae ït quïck!”  But naebodie at tha supper unnèrstud tha raison Jesus toul hïm that.  Seein as Judas lukt eftèr tha siller, yins thocht Jesus wus sennin hïm fer whutiver needit bocht fer tha Faist, or tae gie sumthin tae tha puir.  Sae eftèr Judas haed taen tha bït o breid, awa he went. An ït wus tha blek o nicht. Whaniver Judas went oot, Jesus saed, “Tha Sinn o Man'll noo cum ïntae hïs glorie, an God wull get tha glorie acause o hïm.  An ïf God gets tha glorie on accoont o hïs Sinn, God wull gie glorie tae tha Sinn forbye, an He'll dae ït strecht awa!  Ma dear childèr, A wull be wi yis jist a wee while lang'r. Ye'll be lukkin fer me, an jist laik A toul tha Jews, sae A'm tellin yous noo: ‘Whar A'm fer gaun, yis cannae cum.’  A hae a new commaun tae gie yis: love yin anither. Jist as A hae loved you, that's hoo ye maun love yin anither.  An ïf ye love yin anither, tha hale warl wull see that ye'r ma follaers.” Simon Petèr axt hïm, “Loard, whar ir ye aff tae?” Jesus reponed, “Whar A'm fer, ye cannae follae me noo, but latèr on ye'll follae me.”  Petèr axt, “Loard, hoo cum A cannae follae ye noo? Shair A wud dee fer ye.”  Wi that Jesus answert, “Sae ye'd dee fer me, wud ye? Here's tha truith o ït: afore tha roostèr craas, thrie times ower ye'll say ye dïnnae ken me!” “Dïnnae let yer hairts be sair annoyt. Pit yer trust ïn God, an lippen ïn me forbye.  In ma Faither's hoose thair's monie dwallin-places. If that wusnae richt, A wudnae hae toul ye that A'm gaun tae mak a place readie fer ye, wud A noo?  An whaniver A hae got a place readie fer ye, A'll cum an tak yis bak alang wi me, sae that whar A be, we'll aa be thegither.  Yis ken whar A'm gaun, an yis ken tha róad tae whar A'm gaun.” Tammas turnt an saed til hïm, “Loard, we hae nae notion o whar ye'r fer, sae hoo cud we ken tha róad?”  Jesus reponed, “A be tha róad, an tha truith, an tha life. Naebodie cums tae tha Faither but throu me.  If ye knowed me weel, ye wud ken ma Faither as weel. Frae noo on, yis dae ken hïm an yis hae saa hïm forbye!” Phïlip saed, “Loard, show iz tha Faither an that'll be eneuch fer iz.”  Jesus answert, “Dae ye no ken me Phïlip, tha mair A hae bin amang yis aa thïs time? Oniebodie lukkin at me haes saen tha Faither. Sae hoo can ye say, ‘Show iz tha Faither’?  Phïlip, dae ye no believe that A be ïn tha Faither an tha Faither's ïn me? Tha wurds A'm taakin til yis ir no jist ma ain. Na, ït's tha Faither, leevin ïn me, wha's daein hïs wark.  Tak ma wurd fer ït whaniver A say that A be ïn tha Faither an tha Faither ïs ïn me; or at tha laist, trust me acause o tha warks yis hae saen me daein. Noo here's tha truith o ït, oniebodie that pits thair faith ïn me wull dae tha same warks that A dae. Ay, an he'll dae faur bïgger thïngs ner thon, fer A'm gaun tae be wi ma Faither.  An A'll dae whutiver ye ax ïn ma name, sae as tha Sinn micht brïng glorie til tha Faither.  Ye can ax me fer ocht ïn ma name, an A wull dae ït. If ye love me, ye wull dae whut A bïd ye.  An A wull ax tha Faither, an he wull gie yis an Indwallin Guide, tae be wi yis fer aye -  ït's tha Spïrit o truith A'm taakin aboot. Tha warl cannae tak hïm ïn, fer ït nether sees hïm ner kens hïm. Yous wull ken hïm but, fer he leeves wi ye noo an he'll dwall ïn ye latèr on. A'll no lea yis laik orphan weans; A wull cum tae ye.  Afore lang, tha warl wull no see me nae mair, but yous'll see me. Acause A leeve, yous'll leeve forbye.  Cum thon day, you'll be shair that A be ïn ma Faither, an you ir ïn me, an A am ïn you.  Whaiver taks ma commauns tae hairt an keeps thaim, thon's tha yins that love me. Thaim that love me wull be loved bi ma Faither, an forbye A wull love thaim an show masel tae thaim.”  Wi that Judas - no Judas Iscariot but - he speered, “But Loard, hoo cum ye'r ettlin tae show yersel jist tae iz an no tae tha hale warl?”  Jesus gien tha answer, “If oniebodie loves me, he daes whut he haes lairnt frae me. Ma Faither wull love hïm, an we wull cum tae hïm an mak oor hame wi hïm.  Hïm that daesnae love me wull no dae whut A hae toul hïm. These wurds ye hear ir no ma ain; the' belang tae tha Faither that sent me. A hae toul yis thae thïngs, while A'm still here amang yis.  But tha Indwallin Guide, tha Halie Spïrit, that tha Faither wull senn tae tak ma place, he wull lairn yis aa thïngs an brïng bak tae mine iveriethin A hae toul ye.  Peace A lea wi ye, ma peace A gie ye. A dïnnae gie ye ocht tha wye tha warl gies. Dïnnae let yer hairts be annoyt an dïnnae be afeart.  Ye heerd me tellin ye, ‘A'm leain ye an A'm cumin bak til yis’. If ye loved me, ye wud be gled that A'm fer gaun tae tha Faither, fer tha Faither ïs mair bïgger ner me.  A hae telt ye thïs noo afore ït cums aboot, sae as whaniver ït happens, ye wull believe.  A'm fer taakin tae ye nae mair ner a wee bït lang'r, fer tha prince o thïs warl ïs cumin. He haes nae pooer ower me,  but A'll dae whut aa ma Faither bïds me dae, sae as tha warl micht lairn that A love tha Faither. Weel, cum on noo, we'll be up an awa!” “O a truith, A be tha richt vine. An ma Faither ïs tha gairdner.  He haes iverie brench cut aff o me that haes gien nae fruit. An iverie brench that daes gie fruit he faces bak a weethin sae that ït fruits aa tha mair.  Yous ir aareadie faced on accoont o tha wurd A hae spauk tae ye.  Bide ïn me an A wull bide ïn you. Nae brench can gie fruit ïts lane; ït maun be growein oot o tha vine or ït cannae leeve. An nether can yous gie fruit less ye bide ïn me.  A be tha vine, yous ir tha brenches. If a man bides ïn me, an me ïn hïm, he wull gie fruit ower ocht; apairt frae me ye can dae naethin ava.  If a bodie daesnae bide ïn me, he ïs laik a brench that ïs redd oot an wuthers up an dees; sitch brenches ïs gethert up an coupt ïntae tha fire an brunt.  If ye bide ïn me an ma wurds bide ïn you, ax fer ocht ava ye want, an ït wull be gien til ye.  That's tae tha glorie o ma Faither, that ye'r brustin wi fruit, showin yersels tae be ma follaers.  Jist as tha Faither haes loved me, sae A hae loved you. Bide noo ïn ma love.  If yis dae ma bïddin, ye wull bide ïn ma love, jist laik A masel hae daen ma Faither's bïddin an bide ïn hïs love.  A hae toul ye aa that, sae as ma joy maun be ïn you, ay, an that yer joy maun be fu an skailin. Here's ma commaun. Love yin anither laik A hae loved yous.  Thair's nae bodie haes mair love ner thïs, that he wud dee fer hïs freens.  You ir ma freens ïf ye dae ma bïddin.  Nae mair dae A caa yis sarvints, fer a sarvint daesnae ken ocht o whut hïs maistèr's at. Na, A hae caad yous freens acause iveriethin A hae lairnt frae ma Faither A hae taicht yous as weel.  You dïdnae waal me, na, fer A waaled you, an appointit ye tae gang an bair fruit - fruit that wull last fer aye. An then tha Faither wull gie ye ocht ye ax fer ïn ma name.  Here's whut A bïd ye: love yin anither. If tha warl haits ye, hae mine that ït haitit me furst.  If ye belanged tae tha warl, ït wud love ye as ïts ain. Aa tha same, ye dïnnae belang tae tha warl, but A hae waaled ye oot o tha warl. Thon's tha raison tha warl haits ye.  Hae mine o tha wurds A telt ye: ‘Nae sarvint ïs bïgger ner hïs maistèr.’ If the' haed ït ïn fer me, the'll hae ït ïn fer you forbye. If the' daen ma bïddin, the' wull dae yours as weel.  The'll dail wi ye thon wye acause o ma name, fer the' dïnnae ken tha Yin that sent me.  If A haednae cum an taakt tae thaim, the' wudnae be guiltie o wrangdaein. Hooaniver, the' hae nae caa fer thair sïn noo!  Hïm that haits me haits ma Faither forbye.  If A haednae daen wunnèrfu warks amang thaim laik naebodie else daen, the' wudnae be guiltie o sïn. But the' hae saa thaim, an still an aa, the' hae haitit baith me an ma Faither.  Thïs ïs tae brïng aboot whut ïs writ ïn thair Laa: ‘The' haitit me, an the' haed nae caa fer ït.’  But A'll be sennin yis tha Indwallin Guide frae tha Faither - tha Spïrit o Truith. He'll gang oot frae tha Faither, an whaniver he cums he wull gie wutness aboot me.  An yous maun gie wutness forbye, fer yous hae bin alang wi me richt frae tha verie stairt.” “A telt ye aa thïs sae that yer faith wull no be shuk.  The' wull pit ye oot o tha Meetin Hooses; ay, tha day ïs cumin whan oniebodie that kïlls ye wull thïnk the'r daein God's wark.  An the' wull dae tha laik o thon becas the' hinnae knowed tha Faither ner me.  A hae telt ye thïs, sae as whaniver tha time cums an the' happen, ye'll mine that A gien ye warnin. A dïdnae tell ye at tha stairt, fer A wus still wi ye. Noo A'm awa tae hïm that sent me, an yit nane o yis haes axt me, ‘Whar ir ye aff tae?’  Na, but becas A hae toul yis these thïngs, yer hairts ïs fu o sorra.  But tae tell ye tha truith, ït's fer yer ain guid that A'm gaun awa. Fer less A gang awa, tha halie Guide wull no cum til yis; but ïf A gang, A wull senn hïm tae ye.  Whaniver he cums, he wull show tha warl that ït's ïn tha wrang anent its sïn, anent bein richt, an anent judgemen.  Anent sïn, becas the' dïnnae believe ïn me;  anent bein richt, becas A'm gaun tae tha Faither, whar ye'll no see me onie mair;  an anent judgemen, acause tha prince o thïs warl noo stans condemned bi God. A hae a hale lock mair tae tell ye, mair ner yis cud thole jist noo.  But whaniver tha Spïrit o Truith cums, he wull guide yis ïntae aa tha truith. He'll no spake on hïs ain, he'll tell ye jist whut he hears, an he'll tell ye whut ïs yit tae cum aboot.  He wull brïng glorie tae me bi takkin frae whut ïs mine an makkin ït knowed til yis.  Aa that belangs tae tha Faither ïs mine. Noo, thon's tha raison A telt ye tha Spïrit ïs fer takkin frae whut ïs mine an wull mak ït knowed til ye.” In a wee while ye'll no see me onie mair, an then eftèr anither wee bït, yis wull see me.  Some o tha follaers saed tae yin anither, “Whut's he taakin aboot, ‘In a wee while ye'll see me nae mair, an then eftèr anither wee bït, yis wull see me,’ an, ‘Fer A'm awa tae tha Faither’?”  The kep rhymin, “Whut's he taakin aboot, ‘a wee while’? We dïnnae unnèrstan whut he's on aboot!”  Jesus saa the' wur lukkin tae ax hïm aboot ït aa, sae he saed tae thaim, “Ir ye speerin yin anither aboot me sayin, ‘In a wee while ye'll see me nae mair, an then eftèr anither wee bït, yis wull see me’?  Weel here's tha truith o ït, you wull be greetin an murnin whan tha warl ootbye ïs blythesum. You'll be hairt-sair, but yer sorra wull turn ïntae joy.  A wumman haein a wean ïs wile sair, fer hir time ïs cum; but whaniver hir babbie's boarn, she haes nae mair mine o tha ang'uish acause o hir joy that a wean ïs boarn ïntae tha warl.  Samewyes wi yous: noo's your time o sorra, but A wull see yis agane an yer hairts wull be sïngin fer joy, an naebodie wull tak yer joy awa frae ye.  Cum that day an yis'll no ax me ocht onie mair. Here's tha wye o ït strecht: ma Faither wull gie ye oniethin ye ax fer ïn ma name.  Up tae noo, yis hinnae axt fer ocht ïn ma name. Ax an ye'll hae ït gien, an yer hairts wull be fu o joy. Ma wye o yarnin wi ye aboot these thïngs haes bin tae halp ye pictèr ït aa; tha day ïs cumin that A'll no taak ïn pictèrs onie lang'r, but A'll tell ye strecht aboot ma Faither.  Cum that day, yis'll ax ïn ma name. Noo A'm no sayin A wull then ax tha Faither for ye.  Na, tha Faither hissel loves ye acause yis hae loved me an hae believed that A cum frae God.  Ay, A hae cum frae tha Faither ïntae tha warl; noo A'm leain tha warl an gaun bak tae tha Faither.” Wi that Jesus's follaers saed, “Noo ye'r taakin plain taak wi'oot yarns an pictèrs!  Noo we unnèrstan that you ken iveriethin an that ye hae nae need o fowk quïzzin ye. Frae thïs we believe that ye hae cum frae God.”  “At lang last yis believe!” Jesus answert.  “But tha day wull cum - an ïn fect ït's here noo - whaniver ye'll be skailt, iverie yin o yis tae yer ain hame. Yis'll lea me aa on ma ain. Yit A'm no ma lane, fer ma Faither ïs wi me.  A telt ye aa thon sae that ïn me yis can hae peace. In thïs warl ye wull hae nae enn o bother. But dïnnae be doon-hairtit got. Cheer up! A hae tha warl owercum.” Eftèr these wurds, Jesus lukt up abain tae heiven. “Faither”, he saed, “tha time ïs cum. Gie glorie tae yer Sinn, sae as yer Sinn can gie glorie bak tae yersel.  Fer ye hae gien hïm pooer ower aa tha fowk sae he micht gie ayelastin life tae aa thaim ye hae gien hïm.  Noo thïs ïs ayelastin life: that the' can know you, tha yin true God, an Jesus Christ, that ye hae sent.  A hae brocht ye glorie here on irth bi gettin aa tha wark daen ye gien me fer tae dae.  An noo, Faither, brïng me up ïntae tha glorie A haed wi ye afore tha warl begun.” “A hae made ye known tae thaim that ye gien me oot o thïs warl. The' wur yours, ye gien thaim tae me, an the' hae kep yer wurd.  Noo the' ken that iveriethin A hae frae your han cums frae you o a truith.  Fer A gien thaim tha wurds ye gien tae me an the' tuk thaim tae hairt. Weel the' wut that A cum frae you, an the' believe that ye sent me.  A mak a prayer fer thaim. A'm no prayin fer tha warl, but fer thaim ye hae gien me, fer they belang tae you.  Aa thaimins A hae ïs yours, an aa thaim you hae ïs mine. An glorie ïs cum tae me throu thaim.  A wull bide ïn tha warl nae lang'r, but they ir ïn tha warl yit, an A'm fer cumin tae you. Halie Faither, luk eftèr thaim bi tha pooer o yer name - tha name ye gien me - sae the' can be yin laik we be yin.  Whaniver A wus wi thaim, A lukt eftèr thaim an kep thaim safe an siccar bi tha name ye gien me. Nane haes bin loast apairt frae tha yin duimt tae be desthroyt, sae as whut wus writ ïn tha Scrïptures micht cum aboot.  A'm cumin tae ye richt awa, but A'm taakin aboot thïs jist noo whan A'm still ïn tha warl, sae as the' can hae tha fu meesure o ma joy ïn thair hairts.  A hae gien thaim yer wurd an tha warl haes haitit thaim, fer the'r nae mair o thïs warl ner A be.  Ma prayer ïsnae that ye tak thaim oot o tha warl, but that ye keep thaim safe frae tha wïckit yin.  The'r no o thïs warl, jist laik A'm no o ït.  Set thaim apairt an keep thaim halie bi tha truith; your wurd ïs truith.  Laik ye sent me ïntae tha warl, A hae sent thaim ïntae tha warl.  A set masel apairt fer you on thair accoont, sae as the' can be made perfait halie bi your truith anaa. Ma prayer ïsnae jist fer these follaers thairsels. A mak a prayer forbye fer aa thaim at wull cum tae believe bi wye o thair message;  that the' wull aa be yin, Faither, jist laik you ir ïn me an A be ïn you. Let thaim be ïn iz as weel, sae that tha warl micht believe that ye hae sent me.  A hae gien thaim tha glorie that ye gien me, sae the' can be yin laik we ir yin.  Me ïn thaim, an you ïn me. Let thaim be aa yin thegither as a wutness tae tha hale warl that you sent me, an loved thaim jist laik you hae loved me.  Faither, A'm lukkin fer thaim that ye gien me tae be wi me whar A am tae be, an tae see ma glorie, tha glorie ye hae gien me acause ye loved me afore tha warl wus stairtit.  O Faither, you that aye daes whut's richt, tha mair tha warl daesnae ken ye, A ken ye; an these follaers o mine ken that ye hae sent me.  A hae showed ye tae thaim apenlie, an wull keep on makkin ye knowed tae thaim, sae as tha love ye hae fer me can be ïn thaim an that A can be ïn thaim masel.” Whaniver he wus daen prayin, Jesus tuk hïs follaers athort tha Kidron Glen. On tha ither side thair wus an olive gairden, an hïm an hïs follaers went ïntae ït.  Noo Judas, hïm that wus fer bethrayin hïm, knowed tha place, fer Jesus aye cum thegither thonner wi hïs follaers.  Sae Judas cum tae tha gairden at tha heid o a clatter o sodgers, an Temple gairds sent bi tha heid preeshts an tha Pharisees. The' haed weapons on thaim an the' wur houlin bleezin torches an lamps.  But Jesus knowed fine weel whut aa wus fer happenin tae hïm, sae he cum forrit an axt thaim, “Wha ir ye eftèr?”  “Jesus o Nazareth,” the' reponed. “A be hïm,” qo he. (An Judas tha bethrayer wus stud thonner alang wi thaim.)  Whaniver Jesus saed, “A be hïm,” the' bakt awa an faad tae tha grun.  Yinst mair he axt thaim, “Wha ir ye eftèr?” An the' saed, “Jesus o Nazareth.”  “A toul ye that A be hïm,” Jesus answert. “If ït's me yis ir lukkin fer, then lea these men alane an let thaim gang.”  Noo that aa happent sae as tha wurds he haed spauk wud cum aboot: “A hinnae loast yin o thaim ye gien me.”  Wi that Simon Petèr, that haed a sword on hïm, pued ït oot an hut tha sarvint o tha Heich Preesht, cuttin aff hïs richt lug. (The' caad tha sarvint Malchus.)  Jesus oardèrt Petèr, “Pit yer sword awa ïn ïts skebbard! Shud A no drïnk frae tha bicker tha Faither haes gien me?” An sae tha squad o sodgers wi thair offysher, an tha Temple gairds o tha Jews that wus alang wi thaim, tuk houl o Jesus. The' tyed hïm up,  an furst o aa brocht hïm afore Annas, faither-ïn-laa tae Caiaphas that wus tha Heich Preesht thon yeir.  Caiaphas wus hïm that haed toul tha Jews afore, ït wud be guid ïf yin man wud dee fer tha hale nation. Simon Petèr an anither follaer waakt a wyes behin Jesus. Acause thon follaer wus akwant wi tha Heich Preesht, he wus allooed tae gae wi Jesus ïntae tha verie coortyaird o tha Heich Preesht;  But Petèr haed tae houl on ootbye at tha dure. Tha ither follaer, that wus akwant wi tha Heich Preesht, cum bak oot an haed a wee wurd wi tha lass that wus on tha dure, an brocht Petèr ïn.  “Ye wudnae be yin o hïs follaers, wud ye?” tha sarvin lass on tha dure axt Petèr. He answert, “Na, A'm no.”  Thair wus nae heat ïn tha air, an tha sarvints an tha temple gairds wur stud roon thïs bleeze the' haed lït fer tae keep oot tha coul. Petèr wus stud wi thaim forbye, wairmin hissel. Whan aa thïs wus gaun on, tha Heich Preesht speered Jesus aboot hïs follaers an whut he wus taichin thaim.  “A hae spauk oot ïn tha apen tae yin an aa,” Jesus reponed. “A aye taicht ïn Meetin Hooses or ïn tha Hoose o God, whar aa tha Jews cum thegither. A saed naethin behin shut dures.  Whut ir ye quïzzin me fer? Ax thaim that heerd me. Shair they wud ken whut A saed.”  Whaniver Jesus saed that, yin o tha gairds got ang'rie an he hut hïm on tha face. “Dïnnae taak bak tae tha Heich Preesht laik that!” qo he.  “If A hae saed sumthin wrang,” Jesus saed, “jist tell me whut ït wus. If A wus tellin tha truith but, whut dïd ye hut me fer?”  Still tyed up, Jesus wus sent bi Annas tae Caiaphas tha Heich Preesht. Noo as Simon Petèr wus stud wairmin hissel, the' axt hïm agane, “You wudnae be yin o thaim follaers o hïs, wud ye?” Petèr denied ït tae thair face, sayin, “Na, A'm naethin o tha soart!”  But yin o tha Heich Preesht's sarvints, a freen o tha man that Petèr haed cut tha lug aff, he pued Petèr up an saed, “Dïd A no see ye wi hïm ïn tha olive gairden?”  Yinst mair Petèr denied ït, an at that verie mïnit, a roostèr craad. An sae tha Jews convoyed Jesus frae Caiaphas tae tha palace o tha Roman Guviner. Bi noo ït wus earlie ïn tha moarnin, an sae as tae keep thairsels richt an no be sullied, tha Jews wudnae gang ower tha palace dure; the' wantit tae be fït tae ait tha Passower.  Sae Pilate cum oot tae thaim an axt, “Whut's tha chairges brocht agin thïs man?”  “If he wurnae a laa brekker,” the' answert, “we wudnae a hannit hïm ower til ye.”  Pilate toul thaim, “Tak hïm yersels an judge hïm wi yer ain laas.” “But we hae nae richt tae pit oniebodie tae deith,” tha Jews argyid.  Aa thïs wus saed, sae as tha wurds Jesus haed spauk aboot hoo he wud dee wud cum tae pass. Wi that Pilate went bak ben tha palace, sent fer Jesus, an axt hïm, “Ir you tha Kïng o tha Jews?”  “Wud that be a notion o yer ain?” Jesus answert, “Or haes ithers bin taakin til ye aboot me?”  “Am A a Jew?” Pilate reponed, “It wus yer ain fowk an yer tap preeshts that hannit ye ower til me. Whut ïs ït ye hae daen?”  “Ma kïngdom,” qo Jesus, “ïsnae o thïs warl. If ït wus, ma gairds wud fecht tae stap me bein lïftit an brocht ïn afore tha Jewish heidyins. But na, ma kïngdom ïsnae frae here.”  “Sae ye wud be a kïng, then!” saed Pilate. Jesus answert, “Ye'r richt eneuch sayin A'm a kïng. As a mettèr o fect, tha raison A wus boarn, an fer why A cum ïntae tha warl, wus tae gie wutness tae tha truith. Iveriebodie that's on fer tha truith taks tent o whut A say.”  “An whut wud tha truith be?” axt Pilate. An wi that he went oot agane tae tha Jews an toul thaim, “A can fin nae grun fer a chairge agin hïm.  But yis hae a custom tae ax me tae let yin man oot o jail iverie Passower. Dae yis want me tae let oot ‘tha Kïng o tha Jews’?”  The' yellt oot, “Na, no hïm! Gie iz Barabbas!” Noo Barabbas wus a rebel that haed tuk pairt ïn a risin. Weel, Pilate tuk Jesus awa tae be gien tha whup.  An tha sodgers plettit thoarns thegither tae mak a croon an the' set ït on hïs heid. An the' püt a purple goon on hïm.  An the' kep cumin up tae hïm tae jeer at hïm, “Lang leeve tha Kïng o tha Jews!” An the' skelpt hïm on tha face.  Yinst mair Pilate cum oot an toul tha Jews, “Luk see, A'm brïngin hïm oot til ye an A'm tellin yis agane that A can fin nae gruns fer a chairge agin hïm.”  Wi that, Jesus cum oot, wi tha croon o thoarns an tha purple goon on hïm. An Pilate saed til thaim, “Luk, thïs ïs tha man!”  Tha mïnit tha heid preeshts an tha Temple gairds saa hïm, the' shoutit oot, “Crucyfie hïm! Crucyfie hïm!” But Pilate answert, “Weel, yous can crucyfie hïm yersels, fer A can fin nae gruns fer a chairge agin hïm.”  Tha Jews wudnae budge. “We hae a laa, an owin til thon laa he maun dee, fer he ledged he wus tha Sinn o God.”  Whaniver Pilate heerd that, he wus aa tha mair feart,  an he tuk hissel bak ïntae tha palace. “Whar dae ye cum frae?” he axt Jesus, but Jesus niver saed a wurd.  “Ir you refusin tae taak tae me?” qo Pilate, “Dae ye no unnèrstan A hae tha pooer tae let ye oot or tae nail ye up on a cross?”  Jesus reponed, “Ye wud hae nae pooer ower me, nane ava, ïf ït wusnae gien til ye frae abain. On accoont o that, tha yin that hannit me ower tae ye ïs guiltie o a bïgger sïn.” Frae then on, Pilate ettled at lettin Jesus gang free, but tha Jews kep shoutin, “If ye let thïs man oot, ye'r nae freen o Caesar's. Oniebodie that maks hissel oot tae be a kïng maun be agin Caesar.”  Whaniver Pilate heerd that, he brocht Jesus oot an sut doon on tha judge's sait at a place caad tha Stane Fitpad (ïn tha Aramaic tung, ït gets “Gabbatha”).  Noo ït wus tha day fer makkin readie fer tha Passower sennicht, aboot heich nuin. “Luk, here's yer kïng!” Pilate saed tae tha Jews.  But the' shoutit, “Awa wi hïm! Tak hïm awa! Crucyfie hïm!” “Wull A crucyfie yer kïng?” Pilate axt thaim. “We hae nae kïng but Caesar,” tha heid preeshts answert.  At tha enn o ït aa, Pilate hannit hïm ower tae thaim fer tae be crucyfied. Sae Jesus wus taen awa.  Shoodèrin hïs ain cross, Jesus went oot tae tha Place o tha Skull (thon place the' caa “Golgotha” ïn tha Aramaic tung).  Thonner the' crucyfied hïm alang wi twa ithers - yin on tha yin side, an yin on tha tither, wi Jesus ïn tha mïddle.  Pilate got a wee sign made an püt ït up on tha cross wi thïs writ on ït: “JESUS O NAZARETH, THA KING O THA JEWS.”  Monie o tha Jews haed a read o thon sign, fer tha place whar Jesus wus crucyfied wus nearhan tha cïtie, an tha sign wus writ ïn tha Hebrew, tha Latin an tha Greek.  Tha heid preeshts o tha Jews wurnae plaised, an the' kep on at Pilate, sayin, “Dïnnae jist pit ‘Tha Kïng o tha Jews’ on ït, but pit ‘Thïs man saed he wus the kïng o tha Jews’!”  Pilate answert, “Whut A hae writ, A hae writ.”  Whaniver tha sodgers nailt Jesus on tha cross, the' tuk hïs claes an divïd thaim ïn fower pairts, yin apiece fer each o thaim, wi onlie hïs goon left. Hïs goon wus jist tha yin bït o claith wove frae tap tae bottom, wi nae seams ïn ït.  “We shudnae teer ït up,” the' saed, “Cum on an we'll clod dice fer ït, an see wha gets ït aa.” That happent sae as tha Scrïpture wud cum aboot whar ït wus writ: “The' divïd ma dishables amang thaim, An the' clod dice fer ma claes.” Sae that wus whut tha sodgers daen. Jesus's mither, an hïs mither's sïstèr, an Mary tha guidwife o Clopas, an Mary Magdalene, wur aa stud nixt tha cross that Jesus wus on.  Whaniver Jesus catched sicht o hïs mither thonner, an tha follaer that he loved nearhan, he toul hïs mither, “Guid wumman, thon's yer sinn thonner.”  An tae tha follaer he saed, “An thon's yer mither.” Frae that day an oor, that follaer tuk hir ïntae hïs ain hame. Eftèr thïs, knowin ïn hissel that iveriethin wus noo feenished, an sae as whut wus writ ïn tha Scrïptures micht cum aboot, Jesus saed, “A hae a druith on me.”  A crock o soor wine wus thair, sae the' wat a spongefu, püt tha sponge on a staak o hyssop, an raxt ït up tae Jesus's mooth.  Whaniver he got tha drïnk, Jesus saed, “It's feenished!” Wi that, he bood hïs heid an he gien up hïs spïrit. Noo ït wus tha day o makkin readie fer tha Passower, an tha nixt day bein a bïg, speeshel Sabbath day forbye , tha Jews wur no wantin tha bodies tae bide on tha crosses on tha Sabbath, an sae the' axt Pilate tae hae tha legs brauk an tha bodies tuk doon.  Becas o that, tha sodgers cum an brauk tha legs o tha furst man that wus crucyfied alang wi Jesus, an then tha same thïng wi tha tither.  But whaniver the' cum tae Jesus, an fun oot he wus aareadie deid, the' dïdnae brek hïs legs.  Insteed o that, yin o tha sodgers püsht a pike ïntae Jesus's side, an that brocht oot a flush o bluid an wattèr.  Tha man that saa that happen haes gien wutness o ït, an hïs ïs a true wutness. He kens that he tells tha truith an he gies wutness sae as you micht believe forbye.  Aa thïs happent sae as whut wus writ ïn Scrïpture wud cum aboot: “Nane o hïs banes wull be brauk,”  an as anither pairt o Scrïpture says, “The' wull luk on tha yin the' hae pierced.” Eftèr aa thae thïngs, a man caad Joseph o Arimathea axt Pilate ïf he cud hae tha bodie o Jesus. Noo Joseph wus a follaer, but he kep ït a saicret fer fear o tha Jews. Pilate gien hïm laive, an he cum an tuk tha bodie awa.  An alang wi Joseph wus Nicodemus, hïm that haed cum afore tae Jesus bi nicht. Nicodemus brocht wi hïm a mix o myrrh an aloes, aboot seiventie-five pun wecht.  Takkin Jesus's bodie, tha twa o thaim lapt ït ïn strïps o lïnen claith, thegither wi tha spices. Thïs wus tha rïtual tha Jews aye daen whan the' buriet fowk.  Thonner whar Jesus wus crucyfied, thair wus a gairden, an ïn tha gairden thair wus a new tomb that haed niver bin uised.  Sae seein ït wus tha Jews' Reddin-up day fer tha Passower, an seein as tha tomb wus nearhan, the' haed Jesus layed oot thonner. In tha smaa oors o tha furst day o tha week, whan thair wus nae licht yit, Mary Magdalene cum tae tha tomb an saa that tha stane haed bin taen awa frae tha apenin.  Sae she run bak tae Simon Petèr an tha ither follaer - tha yin Jesus loved - an she saed, “The' hae taen tha Loard oot o tha tomb, an we dïnnae ken whar the' hae püt hïm!”  Sae Petèr an tha ither follaer heidit aff fer tha tomb.  Tha baith o thaim wus rinnin, but tha ither follaer run mair quïck ner Petèr an got tae tha tomb furst.  He stoopit doon an keekt ïn at tha linen claiths lyin thair, but he dïdnae gan ïnbye.  Then Simon Petèr, that wus behin hïm, got thair an went strecht ïntae tha tomb. He saa tha strïps o linen lyin thonner,  forbye tha buryin cloot that haed bin roon Jesus's heid. But tha cloot wus lapt up bi ïtsel, awa frae tha linen.  Sae noo tha ither follaer, that haed got tae tha tomb furst, went inside tae. He saa iveriethin, an he believed.  (The' dïdnae unnèrstan yit frae tha halie Scrïptures that Jesus wud hae tae rise frae tha deid.)  Wi that tha follaers went bak tae thair hames. But Mary stud ootbye tha tomb greetin. An whan she wus greetin, she stoopit doon fer tae tak a luk inside tha tomb.  An she saa twa angels ïn white claes, sut whar Jesus's bodie haed bin, yin at tha heid an tha tither at tha fit.  The' axt hir, “Wumman, whut ir ye greetin fer?” “The' hae taen ma Loard awa,” qo she, “an A dïnnae ken whar the' hae püt hïm.”  Sayin that, she turnt roon an saa Jesus stud thonner, but she dïdnae twig that ït wus Jesus.  “Wumman,” qo he, “Whut ir ye greetin fer? Wha ïs ït ye'r lukkin?” She thocht ït wus tha gairdner, an she saed, “Sïr, ïf ye hae cairriet hïm awa, tell iz whar ye hae püt hïm, an A'll get hïm.”  Jesus saed til hir, “Mary!” She turnt roon tae hïm an caad oot, “Rabboni!” (that mains “Dominie” ïn tha Aramaic).  Jesus saed, “Dïnnae be hingin ontae me noo, fer A'm no yit gan bak tae tha Faither. But gang tae ma brithers an tell thaim thïs frae me: ‘A'm fer gaun bak tae ma Faither, an tae your Faither, tae ma God an tae your God’.”  Mary Magdalene went tae fin tha follaers an tell thaim tha guid news, “A hae saa tha Loard!” An she toul thaim whut he haed saed til hir. Whaniver ït wus dairk got on thon furst day o tha week, tha follaers wur thegither behin lockt dures fer fear o tha Jews. An Jesus cum an stud amang thaim. “Peace be wi yis!” qo he.  An eftèr sayin thïs, he showed thaim hïs hans an hïs side. Tha follaers wus fu o joy whaniver the' saa tha Loard.  Agane Jesus saed, “Peace be wi yis! Jist as tha Faither haes sent me, A'm sennin yous as weel.”  An wi that he breathed ower thaim an he saed, “Tak tha Halie Spïrit tae yersels!  If ye forgie oniebodie thair sïns, the'll be forgien; ïf ye dïnnae forgie thaim the'r no forgien.” Noo Tammas (that the' caad Didymus), yin o tha Twal, wusnae alang wi tha ither follaers whaniver Jesus cum.  Sae tha ither follaers toul hïm, “We hae saa tha Loard!” But he saed til thaim, “Less A behoul tha mairks o tha nails ïn hïs hans an pit ma fïng'r whar tha nails wus, an less A pit ma han ïntae hïs side, A'll niver believe ït!” A sennicht latèr tha follaers wus ïn tha hoose agane, an thïs time Tammas wus wi thaim. Tha mair tha dures wus lockt, Jesus cum an stud amang thaim an saed, “Peace be wi yis!”  An then he saed tae Tammas, “Pit yer fïng'r here. Hae a luk at ma hans. Rax oot yer han an pit ït ïntae ma side. An quït yer dootin an believe!”  Tammas saed til hïm, “Ma Loard an ma God!”  Jesus telt hïm, “Acause ye hae saa me, ye hae believed; weel fer thaim that haesnae saa, but haes believed aa tha same.” Noo Jesus wrocht a hale wheen o ither mïraclis signs ïn front o hïs follaers that's no bin recoardit ïn thïs here buik.  But these yins ir püt doon sae yis can lippen that Jesus ïs tha Christ, tha Sinn o God, an that bi believin ye can hae life throu hïm. Latèr on, Jesus appeart agane tae hïs follaers, thïs time on tha loch shore o Tiberias . Here's hoo ït happent.  Simon Petèr, Tammas (caad Didymus, tha twun), Nathaniel frae Cana ïn Galilee an tha sinns o Zebedee wur aa thegither thonner, wi twa ither follaers.  “A'm awa oot tae ketch some fïsh,” Simon Petèr toul thaim, an the' saed, “We'll gang alang wi ye.” Sae oot the' went an got ïntae tha bóat, but the' niver catched ocht ava tha hale nicht. In tha smaa oors o tha moarnin, Jesus wus stud on tha shore, but tha follaers dïdnae ken ït wus hïm.  Jesus caad oot tae thaim, “Freens, hae yis no catched onie fïsh?” “Na,” the' reponed.  “Pit yer neyt oot,” qo he, “on tha richt-han side o tha bóat an yis'll fin some.” Whaniver the' dïd, the' wurnae fït tae pu ïn tha neyt, thair wus that monie fïsh ïn ït!  An then tha follaer that Jesus loved saed tae Petèr, “It's tha Loard, sae ït ïs!” Tha mïnit Simon Petèr heerd hïm say, “It's tha Loard,” he lapt hïs ooter claes roon hissel - fer he haed taen thaim aff fer fïshin - an he lep ïntae tha wattèr.  Tha ither follaers cum alang behin hïm ïn tha bóat, pu'in tha neyt fu o fïsh, fer the' wurnae faur frae shore, nae mair ner a hunnèr yairds. Whaniver the' lannit, the' saa a fire o bleezin coals thonner wi fïsh on ït, an some breid.  Jesus saed til thaim, “Brïng some o thaim fïsh ye hae jist catched.”  Simon Petèr climmed aboord an dregged tha neyt tae tha shore. It wus fu o bïg fïsh, a hunnèr an fïftie-thrie o thaim, but tha mair ït haed sae monie, ït wusnae tore.  Jesus saed tae thaim, “Cum on an hae yer brekfast.” Nane o tha follaers dar ax hïm, “Wha ir ye?” The' knowed ït wus tha Loard.  Jesus cum, tuk tha breid an gien ït tae thaim, an he daen tha same wi tha fïsh.  Noo thïs wus tha thurd time Jesus haed appeart tae hïs follaers eftèr he wus ris frae tha deid. Whaniver the' wur daen aitin, Jesus saed tae Simon Petèr, “Simon, sinn o Jhone, dae ye love me mair ner aa these ither yins dae?” “Ay Loard,” qo he, “ye ken that A love ye.” Jesus saed, “Luk eftèr ma lambs.”  Agane Jesus saed, “Simon, sinn o Jhone, dae ye love me?” He answert, “Ay, Loard, ye ken that A love ye.” Jesus saed, “Tak guid care o ma sheep.”  Tha thurd time he saed til hïm, “Simon, sinn o Jhone, dae ye love me?” Petèr wus hurt that Jesus axt hïm tha thrie times, “Dae ye love me?” He saed, “Loard, ye ken iveriethin; ye ken that A love ye.” Jesus saed, “Luk eftèr ma sheep.  Noo here's tha truith o ït. Whan ye wur a young yin, ye püt yer ain claes on bi yersel an ye went whariver ye wantit; but whaniver ye'r oul got ye'll rax oot yer hans an some ither bodie wull pit yer claes on ye, an tak ye whar ye dïnnae want tae gang.”  Jesus saed that fer tae point oot tha wye Petèr wud dee, an hoo he wud brïng glorie tae God. An then he saed til hïm, “Follae me!” Petèr lukt ower hïs shoodèr an saa tha follaer that Jesus loved cumin eftèr thaim - tha yin that haed leant bak agin Jesus at tha supper an axt, “Loard, wha's gaun tae bethray ye?”  Whaniver Petèr saa that follaer, he axt, “Loard, whut aboot hïm?”  Jesus answert, “If A want hïm tae leeve richt up tae tha day A cum bak, whut's ït tae dae wi you? Jist you follae me.”  On accoont o thïs, tha taak went roon tha brithers that thïs follaer wudnae dee. But Jesus niver saed that he wudnae dee; he jist saed, “If A want hïm tae leeve richt up tae tha day A cum bak, whut's ït tae dae wi you?” Thon follaer ïs tha yin that gies wutness tae aa these thïngs an writ thaim doon. We can be shair hïs testimonie ïs true. Jesus daen monie ither thïngs forbye. If iverie yin o thaim wus writ doon, A jalouse that even tha hale warl wudnae hae ruim eneuch fer aa tha buiks that wud be scrievit.
